My attack here is:

1. **Prove the centered-to-patch descent lemma.**  
Start from the centered symmetric-placement variable \(s\), where the current package gives
\[
u_5,\ v_5,\ u_{7,K_1},\ v_{7,K_1}\ \text{odd in }s,\qquad \Delta_7\ \text{even in }s,
\]
with explicit low-order coefficients \(U_j,V_j,\widehat U_j,\widehat V_j,D_2,D_4,D_6\). The key task is to make rigorous that, on the relevant mixed local regime, the good-patch coordinate
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c}
\]
is an odd local coordinate in \(s\) with odd inverse. That is the bridge everything depends on. turn10file12turn11file14

2. **Push parity through that coordinate change.**  
If that lemma is true, then the centered parity transfers into the \(x\)-chart:
\[
Y=\frac{u_5}{c}\ \text{odd},\qquad
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}\ \text{odd},\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{cv_5}\ \text{odd}.
\]
Hence
\[
Y''\ \text{odd},\qquad S''\ \text{odd},\qquad
\mathcal Z=\frac{Y''}{S''}\ \text{even},\qquad
\mathcal R=\mathcal Z'\ \text{odd},\qquad
K_v=(x')^3S''\ \text{odd}.
\]
That is the actual parity package I am trying to turn into theorem-level closure. turn10file5turn10file13

3. **Use that parity package to kill the explicit mixed low-order bad list.**  
The mixed dangerous cases have already been reduced to
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}.
\]
But under the transferred parity package, \(r=\ord_0K_v\) must be odd and \(\ord_0\mathcal Z\) must be even. That rules out all three patterns immediately. So the mixed low-order branch should collapse once the descent lemma is nailed down. turn10file13

4. **Not spend time trying to kill the nonmixed branch from lifted variables alone.**  
I do **not** think that is the right use of this thread. The nonmixed side is organized by
\[
\mathcal Z=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda},\qquad
\mathcal R=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2},
\]
and the dangerous nonmixed cases are
\[
\ord_0\mathcal R\in\{1,3,5\}.
\]
The realization/no-go result says no identity involving only \((c,v_5,u_5,\Delta_7)\) and derivatives can exclude those patterns in general. So that branch really belongs to the other chat’s deeper source-/matrix-level attack. turn11file11turn11file14

So, stated as plainly as possible:

**My job here is to prove that the centered \(s\)-parity really descends through \(x=v_5/c\), and then use it to eliminate the whole mixed low-order \(4\)-point obstruction list.**  
**The other chat’s job is to find the deeper RH-specific structure needed for the nonmixed branch and the source-level factorization route.** turn11file13

Now I’m going to attack the descent lemma itself.

_Thought for 5m 15s_

I attacked the mixed bridge, and the strongest clean thing I can now say is this:

**the mixed low-order branch is rigorously dead as soon as the centered variable really induces an odd good-patch coordinate.**

More precisely, here is the theorem hiding inside your current route.

**Proposition.**  
Let \(s\) be the centered symmetric-placement variable. Assume near \(s=0\) that
\[
c(s)=C_0+C_2s^2+C_4s^4+\cdots,\qquad C_0\neq 0,
\]
\[
u_5(s),\ v_5(s)\ \text{odd},\qquad \Delta_7(s)\ \text{even},
\]
and \(V_1\neq 0\) in
\[
v_5(s)=V_1s+V_3s^3+V_5s^5+\cdots.
\]
Define
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{cv_5}=\frac{\lambda}{c}.
\]
Then:

1. \(x(s)\) is odd with odd local inverse \(s(x)\);
2. \(Y(x)\), \(\lambda(x)\), and \(S(x)\) are odd;
3. hence
\[
Y''(x)\ \text{odd},\qquad S''(x)\ \text{odd},
\]
so
\[
\mathcal Z(x)=\frac{Y''}{S''}\ \text{even},\qquad
\mathcal R(x)=\mathcal Z'(x)\ \text{odd};
\]
4. and because
\[
K_v=(x')^3S'' ,
\]
with \(x'(s)\) even, \(K_v\) is odd as a germ in \(s\), hence odd in \(x\).

From this, the whole explicit mixed low-order bad list is impossible.

Here is the clean proof.

Since \(v_5\) is odd and \(c\) is even, \(x=v_5/c\) is odd. Because \(X_1=V_1/C_0\neq 0\), it is a local coordinate, and its inverse \(s(x)\) is odd. Then
\[
Y=\frac{u_5}{c}
\]
is odd divided by even, so odd in \(s\), hence odd in \(x\). Likewise
\[
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}
\]
is even divided by odd, hence odd in \(s\), and therefore odd in \(x\). Since \(c\) is even, \(S=\lambda/c\) is also odd in \(x\).

Now an odd germ differentiated twice is odd, so \(Y''\) and \(S''\) are odd. Their quotient is therefore even, and one more derivative makes \(\mathcal R\) odd.

For the mixed branch, the local model is
\[
Q_v(x)\sim (x^n,\ x,\ x^m),\qquad n>m\ge 3.
\]
But if both \(Y\) and \(S\) are odd germs, then their first nonzero orders \(n\) and \(m\) must both be odd. So the three currently dangerous mixed patterns
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6)
\]
are impossible immediately.

Equivalently, since
\[
r=\operatorname{ord}_0 K_v = m-2,
\qquad
\operatorname{ord}_0\mathcal Z = n-m,
\]
we get
\[
r\ \text{odd},\qquad \operatorname{ord}_0\mathcal Z\ \text{even},
\]
which rules out
\[
(r,\operatorname{ord}_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}.
\]

So that part is now clean.

What remains is much narrower than before. It is not “prove the whole mixed theorem from scratch.” It is just:

- prove that in the actual centered normalization stack, the cubic scalar \(c\) is even in the centered variable \(s\);
- check that the relevant collision-side regime really has \(V_1\neq 0\), which is exactly the condition that \(x=v_5/c\) is a genuine local coordinate there.

Once those two points are in, the mixed low-order exclusion is no longer heuristic. It is a theorem.

There is also a slightly stronger way to phrase the same result:

if the centered-to-patch transfer holds, then the mixed branch is not merely constrained by parity of \(\mathcal Z\) and \(K_v\); the mixed branch is forced into an **odd/odd local model**
\[
Q_v(x)\sim (x^n,\ x,\ x^m),\qquad m,n\ \text{odd}.
\]
That is stronger than just saying the list \((1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\) is excluded.

My honest read is that this is the real progress from the attack:
the mixed low-order branch is not “probably false.” It is **conditionally finished**, with a very small remaining proof obligation.

The nonmixed side is unchanged by this attack. The same parity package gives
\[
\mathcal Z \text{ even},\qquad \mathcal R \text{ odd},
\]
which is perfectly compatible with
\[
\operatorname{ord}_0\mathcal R\in\{1,3,5\},
\]
so it does nothing to the nonmixed bad list. That still belongs to the other chat’s deeper source-/matrix-level route.

So the exact status after this attack is:

- mixed low-order \(4\)-point branch: conditionally closed, pending the evenness of \(c(s)\) in the actual centered normalization;
- nonmixed \(4\)-point branch: still genuinely open and still below the current lifted-variable package.

If you want, next I would attack the single remaining local question directly: **why should \(c(s)\) be even under the centered swap symmetry in the actual normalization stack?** That is now the bottleneck for this thread.

## Assistant (2026-04-20 07:52:06)

I’m now attacking the one real bottleneck for this thread: whether the centered swap symmetry in the actual normalization forces \(c(s)\) to be even. If that goes through, the mixed branch really does collapse.

_Thought for 3m 31s_

I attacked the bottleneck, and I think the right conclusion is:

**the real missing lemma is not a mysterious parity fact about \(c\); it is an equivariant cubic-normalization lemma. Once you have that, \(c(s)\) even is automatic.**

Here is the clean argument.

In the centered variable \(s\), the microscopic swap is \(s\mapsto -s\). Your current centered package already records the target parity pattern
\[
c(s)\ \text{even},\qquad u_5(s),v_5(s)\ \text{odd},\qquad \Delta_7(s)\ \text{even},
\]
and the later bridge formulas for \(x=v_5/c\), \(Y=u_5/c\), \(\lambda=\Delta_7/v_5\), and \(S=\Delta_7/(cv_5)\) are already written in exactly the form needed for the mixed attack. turn21file5turn21file6

What I wanted was the conceptual reason for that evenness of \(c\), not just the formal expansion. I think it is this.

Let \(\Sigma\) be the swap involution on odd germs,
\[
\Sigma(F)(z):=J_0\,F(-z)\,J_0.
\]
The quotient-germ side of the draft/convo already uses this involution, and on the cubic-generic region one may choose the cubic representative in the diagonal-traceless direction
\[
A_3=c\,D,\qquad D=\begin{pmatrix}1&0\\0&-1\end{pmatrix},
\]
with \(J_0DJ_0=-D\). The same notes also push the point that admissible normalized germs should preserve the swap symmetry on the quotient-germ side. turn21file11

Now suppose the centered family of normalized one-pair germs is chosen equivariantly, i.e.
\[
F_{-s}=\Sigma(F_s)=J_0\,F_s(-z)\,J_0.
\]
Write the cubic coefficient as
\[
F_s(z)=A_3(s)z^3+\cdots,\qquad A_3(s)=c(s)\,D.
\]
Comparing \(z^3\)-coefficients gives
\[
A_3(-s)=-J_0A_3(s)J_0.
\]
But since \(A_3(s)=c(s)D\) and \(J_0DJ_0=-D\),
\[
-J_0A_3(s)J_0
=
-c(s)J_0DJ_0
=
-c(s)(-D)
=
c(s)D.
\]
Hence
\[
A_3(-s)=A_3(s),
\]
so
\[
c(-s)=c(s).
\]

That is the whole point. The evenness of \(c\) is not an extra miracle. It is forced by:

- centered swap equivariance of the normalized family, and
- the fact that the cubic line is represented by an anti-fixed diagonal-traceless matrix \(D\). turn21file11

Once that is in place, the rest of the mixed bridge is no longer slippery.

Since \(v_5(s)\) is odd and \(c(s)\) is even,  
\[
x(s)=\frac{v_5(s)}{c(s)}
\]
is odd. If \(V_1\neq 0\), it is a local odd coordinate with odd inverse. Since \(\Delta_7(s)\) is even, one gets
\[
Y(x)=\frac{u_5}{c}(x)\ \text{odd},\qquad
\lambda(x)=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}(x)\ \text{odd},\qquad
S(x)=\frac{\Delta_7}{cv_5}(x)\ \text{odd}.
\]
Therefore
\[
Y''(x),S''(x)\ \text{odd},\qquad
\mathcal Z=\frac{Y''}{S''}\ \text{even},\qquad
\mathcal R=\mathcal Z'\ \text{odd},\qquad
K_v=(x')^3S''\ \text{odd}.
\]
And that kills the explicit mixed low-order bad list
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\},
\]
because \(r=\ord_0K_v\) must be odd while \(\ord_0\mathcal Z\) must be even. turn20file6turn21file6

So the attack result is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Mixed low-order closure reduces to one equivariant-normalization lemma.}
}
\]

Not to a new parity computation. Not to more Taylor algebra.

The one lemma you need is something like:

**Equivariant cubic normalization in centered symmetric placement.**  
In the centered symmetric-placement family, the admissible normalized one-pair quotient germ can be chosen so that
\[
F_{-s}=\Sigma(F_s)=J_0F_s(-z)J_0
\]
and its cubic coefficient is represented continuously as
\[
A_3(s)=c(s)D
\]
with fixed anti-fixed \(D\).

Then \(c(s)\) is even automatically, and the mixed centered-to-patch parity bridge becomes theorem-level.

My honest assessment is that this is a real narrowing of the problem. The mixed branch is no longer blocked by a vague coordinate issue. It is blocked by one specific structural bridge: **does the actual normalization stack preserve centered swap equivariance at the quotient-germ level?**

If yes, the mixed low-order branch is finished.

If you want the next move here, I would now write that equivariant-normalization lemma explicitly and check it against the draft’s allowed normalization operations one by one: scalar renormalization, cubic normalization choice, and any symmetry-preserving basis changes.

\[

\[
A_5^{\mathrm{new}}=A_5+c_2A_3+[B_2,A_3].
\]
So any centered-parity theorem does **not** need a brand-new jet computation. It only needs a symmetry statement saying the admissible ambiguity class is stable under the centered swap involution. That is the exact right structural target. turn26file13

The second solid point is that the paper really does already contain a built-in swap symmetry from symmetric placement. On the finite-\(s\) side it appears as
\[
\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(-s;m)=J_0\,\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m)\,J_0,
\]
and on the quotient-germ side it is formalized by
\[
\Sigma(F)(z):=J_0F(-z)J_0.
\]
In the quintic package this makes the cubic-normalized raw corrected quintic slice anti-fixed:
\[
J_0A_5J_0=-A_5.
\]
So there is real involutive structure in the file; that part is not wishful thinking. turn26file9turn26file10

But here is the correction: **this is not yet the symmetry you need for the dream mixed-parity package.** The other chat’s matrix-level push is right about that. The symmetry already in the draft acts on the raw quintic coefficient by the anti-fixed representation, but that alone does **not** imply the centered-source parity package
\[
c(s)\ \text{even},\qquad u_5(s),v_5(s)\ \text{odd},\qquad \Delta_7(s)\ \text{even}
\]
for the fixed-sector scalars as functions of the centered parameter \(s\). In other words, the existing swap involution is real, but it is the **wrong symmetry by itself** for the conclusion we want. turn26file10

So my honest update is:

My previous reduction “mixed branch closes once \(c(s)\) is even” was directionally right, but still one layer too optimistic.

What is actually needed is a stronger theorem of this form:

**centered equivariance descends through the whole ambiguity/normalization/fixed-sector pipeline.**

Concretely, the next theorem to try to prove is:

Let \(V_s\) be the ambiguity space through the relevant order in the centered symmetric-placement family. Show that it is \(\Sigma\)-stable, that the centered raw corrected class is \(\Sigma\)-fixed, and that after cubic normalization plus fixed-sector projection, the induced centered family still transforms equivariantly under \(s\mapsto -s\). Only then can one read off parity of \(c,u_5,v_5,\Delta_7\). turn26file9

That is now the exact attack point for this thread.

If that stronger descent theorem does go through, then the payoff is still exactly what we wanted: the centered-to-patch bridge would force
\[
\mathcal Z=\frac{Y''}{S''}\ \text{even},\qquad K_v\ \text{odd},
\]
and that would kill the explicit mixed low-order obstruction list
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}.
\]
So the mixed branch is still plausibly killable this way; it is just **not yet justified by the currently recorded swap symmetry alone**. turn25file2

And the nonmixed side is unchanged by this attack. The local affine and lifted analyses still say generic local geometry is too flexible there, so the nonmixed branch remains a deeper source-/matrix-level problem, which matches the division of labor you set up between this thread and the convo10 thread. turn25file1turn26file10

The mixed route is still alive.

The current centered package already gives

which kills the explicit mixed low-order list
\[

The draft still labels this as provisional because it had not pinned down the \(c(s)\)-parity / \(x(s)\)-oddness step cleanly enough. turn30file2turn30file18

I think that missing step can actually be supplied, at least in the centered diagonal-based regime.

The reason is that the file’s normalization is not arbitrary there: it explicitly introduces the involution
\[
\Sigma(F)(z)=J_0F(-z)J_0
\]
and defines the cubic-normalized raw germ so that the cubic normalization preserves the swap symmetry inherited from symmetric placement. It also already proves that, through order \(5\), the quotient-level ambiguity sits in the \(J_0\)-anti-fixed sector. turn31file9

Now in the centered symmetric-placement variable \(s\), let the cubic coefficient of the normalized one-pair germ be
\[
A_3(s)=c(s)\,D,
\qquad
D=\begin{pmatrix}1&0\\0&-1\end{pmatrix}.
\]
This is the right form because the cubic leading line is diagonal-traceless, hence \(D\)-directional in the cubic-generic region. Under the swap involution,
\[
A_3(-s)=-J_0A_3(s)J_0.
\]
But \(J_0DJ_0=-D\), so
\[
A_3(-s)=-J_0(c(s)D)J_0
=-c(s)(-D)
=c(s)D.
\]
Therefore
\[
c(-s)=c(s).
\]
So the evenness of \(c\) is not an extra hypothesis; it is forced by the centered swap-equivariant cubic normalization. turn31file9

Once you insert that into the centered Taylor package, the rest is formal. Since \(v_5(s)\) is odd and \(c(s)\) is even,
\[
x(s)=\frac{v_5(s)}{c(s)}
\]
is odd. If \(V_1\neq 0\), it is a local odd coordinate with odd inverse \(s(x)\). Since \(\Delta_7(s)\) is even,
\[
\lambda(s)=\frac{\Delta_7(s)}{v_5(s)}
\]
is odd, hence
\[
Y(x)=\frac{u_5}{c}(x),\qquad
S(x)=\frac{\Delta_7}{cv_5}(x)=\frac{\lambda}{c}(x)
\]
are odd in \(x\). Then
\[
Y''(x),\,S''(x)\ \text{are odd},
\]
so
\[
\mathcal Z(x)=\frac{Y''}{S''}\ \text{is even},\qquad
\mathcal R(x)=\mathcal Z'(x)\ \text{is odd},\qquad
K_v=(x')^3S''\ \text{is odd}.
\]
That is exactly the parity package you wanted on the mixed side. turn31file12

And then the low-order mixed obstruction list dies immediately:
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)=(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)
\]
is impossible because \(\ord_0 K_v=r\) must be odd, while \(\ord_0\mathcal Z\) must be even. So \((1,1)\) and \((1,3)\) fail by parity of \(\mathcal Z\), and \((2,2)\) fails by parity of \(K_v\). turn31file12

So the strongest attack result I can honestly claim is this:

**In the centered diagonal-based regime, the mixed low-order \(4\)-point branch is already locally excluded.** The only remaining issue is not the local parity algebra anymore; it is promotion from that centered diagonal regime to the full general good-patch geometry. _Thought for 4m 52s_

Here is the strongest clean attack result I think we have now.

## Local theorem at the centered diagonal base

Work in the centered collision-side coordinate
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\]
in the diagonal-based local regime where the centered symmetric-placement package really gives
\[
c(s)\ \text{even},\qquad
u_5(s),v_5(s)\ \text{odd},\qquad
\Delta_7(s)\ \text{even},
\]
so that after transfer to the induced odd coordinate \(x\),
\[
Y(x)=\frac{u_5}{c}(x)\ \text{odd},\qquad
\lambda(x)=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}(x)\ \text{odd},\qquad
S(x)=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}(x)\ \text{odd}.
\]
This is exactly the centered-diagonal package recorded in the attached notes. turn37file11turn37file13

Now do the affine normalizations that are already standard in this branch: subtract the linear part of \(S\), and subtract from \(Y\) its component in \(\operatorname{span}\{1,x,S\}\). Because oddness is preserved, one gets
\[
S(x)=a_m x^m+a_{m+2}x^{m+2}+\cdots,\qquad m\ge 3\ \text{odd},\ a_m\neq 0,
\]
\[
Y(x)=b_n x^n+b_{n+2}x^{n+2}+\cdots,\qquad n>m,\ n\ \text{odd},\ b_n\neq 0.
\]
So the centered base is automatically in an odd/odd mixed model; in particular the nonmixed cases \(n=4,6,8\) and the explicit mixed low-order bad cases \((m,n)=(3,4),(3,6),(4,6)\) are already excluded at the base itself. turn37file3turn37file4

Now differentiate:
\[
S''(x)=x^{m-2}\Sigma(x^2),\qquad \Sigma(0)=m(m-1)a_m\neq 0,
\]
\[
Y''(x)=x^{n-2}J(x^2),\qquad J(0)=n(n-1)b_n\neq 0.
\]
Hence
\[
\mathcal Z(x):=\frac{Y''}{S''}=x^{\,n-m}\Xi(x^2),\qquad \Xi(0)\neq 0.
\]
Since \(n-m\) is a positive even integer, \(\mathcal Z\) is even and vanishes to even order at \(0\). Differentiating once,
\[
\mathcal R(x):=\mathcal Z'(x)=x^{\,n-m-1}\Lambda(x^2),\qquad \Lambda(0)\neq 0.
\]
So \(\mathcal R\) is odd and, crucially, has no zeros for sufficiently small nonzero \(x\). This is the structural reason the explicit mixed low-order list dies in this regime. It is stronger than parity bookkeeping alone. turn37file1turn37file2

Now use the exact lifted identities from the branch:
\[
K_v=(x')^3S'',
\qquad
T_v=(x')^6\bigl(S''Y'''-S'''Y''\bigr)
      =(x')^6(S'')^2\mathcal R.
\]
Because \(x'(0)\neq 0\), the factors \(x'\), \(\Sigma(x^2)\), and \(\Lambda(x^2)\) stay nonzero on a sufficiently small punctured neighborhood of \(0\). Therefore there exists \(\varepsilon>0\) such that
\[
0<|x|<\varepsilon
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
K_v(x)\neq 0,\qquad T_v(x)\neq 0.
\]
So the centered diagonal base has a punctured neighborhood containing **no further mixed points** and **no nearby nonmixed \(T_v=0\) points** at all. The basepoint itself is mixed; everything nearby is sterile. turn37file2turn37file4turn37file7

That is the clean theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{In the centered diagonal odd/odd regime, the basepoint is an isolated mixed point and the punctured neighborhood is free of }K_v=0\text{ and }T_v=0.
}
\]

## Generic lowest-order case

In the generic centered case
\[
S(x)=ax^3+bx^5+\cdots,\qquad
Y(x)=px^5+qx^7+\cdots,\qquad a,p\neq 0,
\]
one gets explicitly
\[
\mathcal Z(x)=\frac{10p}{3a}x^2+\left(\frac{7q}{a}-\frac{100bp}{9a^2}\right)x^4+O(x^6),
\]
\[
\mathcal R(x)=\frac{20p}{3a}x+\left(\frac{28q}{a}-\frac{400bp}{9a^2}\right)x^3+O(x^5).
\]
So \(\mathcal R(x)\neq 0\) for all sufficiently small nonzero \(x\). This is the explicit coefficient version of the same local sterility statement. 

## What this actually buys us

This is a real advance, because it proves the dangerous low-order patterns are **not born at first contact from the centered diagonal base**. If they exist anywhere, they must arise only after transporting away from that base and then recentering at a nonzero point. The notes already identify that next perturbative target: for \(x_0\neq 0\), one is generically in the nonmixed regime since \(S''(x_0)\neq 0\), and the obstruction becomes zeros of the even function \(Y'''(x_0)\), appearing in symmetric \(\pm x_0\) pairs. turn37file4

So the frontier is now much narrower:

- We have a genuine **local centered-diagonal exclusion theorem**.
- The remaining mixed-branch question is a **transport/recentering question**, not a basepoint-parity question.
- The nonmixed branch still belongs to the deeper route, exactly as your split with the other chat says. turn37file13turn37file14

The next natural attack from here is to compute the recentered jets at \(x=x_0+\eta\) and see whether the first even terms that appear off the diagonal can actually realize one of the dangerous patterns, or whether they are still blocked by additional structure.

## Finite-jet bridge lemma

\[

\qquad

\]
on the relevant centered good patch.

\[

\]
has no \(x^1\) or \(x^3\) term, killing \((1,1)\) and \((1,3)\), while \(S''\) has odd vanishing order, killing \((2,2)\). That is exactly the other chat’s finite-jet sharpening, and I think it is the right target now.

If
\[
f(s)=f_1s+f_3s^3+f_5s^5+O(s^7)
\]
is any odd \(6\)-jet, and
\[
x(s)=X_1s+X_3s^3+X_5s^5+O(s^7),\qquad X_1\neq 0,
\]

\[
s(x)=\frac1{X_1}x-\frac{X_3}{X_1^4}x^3+\frac{3X_3^2-X_1X_5}{X_1^7}x^5+O(x^7),
\]
and composing gives
\[
f(x)=\frac{f_1}{X_1}x+\frac{X_1f_3-X_3f_1}{X_1^4}x^3
+\frac{X_1^2f_5-3X_1X_3f_3+(3X_3^2-X_1X_5)f_1}{X_1^7}x^5
+O(x^7).
\]
So **oddness through order \(6\) is automatic under odd reparametrization**. There are no \(x^2,x^4,x^6\) terms to check separately.

That is the key attack result.

\[
Y(s)=\frac{u_5(s)}{c(s)},\qquad
S(s)=\frac{\Delta_7(s)}{c(s)v_5(s)}.

\[

and an explicit \(b_5\) as well.

\[
Y(x)=a_1x+a_3x^3+a_5x^5+O(x^7),
\qquad
S(x)=\beta_1x+\beta_3x^3+\beta_5x^5+O(x^7),
\]
with no even terms. In fact the first coefficients are
\[

\]

\beta_3=\frac{C_0^2(D_4V_1-2D_2V_3)}{V_1^5}.
\]

That means the other chat’s finite-jet lemma is already proved modulo the single bridge input:
\[
Y,S \text{ odd mod } O(x^7).
\]

And from there the mixed low-order exclusion is immediate. Differentiating,
\[
Y''(x)=6a_3x+20a_5x^3+O(x^5),\qquad
S''(x)=6\beta_3x+20\beta_5x^3+O(x^5),
\]
so
\[
\mathcal Z(x)=\frac{Y''}{S''}
\]
has only even powers through the relevant order, and
\[
K_v=(x')^3S''
\]
has odd vanishing order. Therefore the explicit mixed bad list
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}
\]
is impossible. That is exactly the mixed obstruction list both chats isolated.  

So the status is now tighter than before:

- the diagonal centered base is locally sterile; that part still stands. 
- the determinant route and the parity route are now saying the same thing. 
- and the mixed low-order branch is no longer blocked by some messy coefficient algebra.

It is blocked by exactly one input:

\[

\]

_Thought for 2m 20s_

Here is the cleanest thing I can now attack and actually sharpen.

The phrase “branch-identification theorem” has been carrying two different issues, and only one of them is real.

The **first issue** is whether the centered symmetric-placement germ and the later good-patch germ are the same local \(1\)-parameter family. Locally, in the diagonal-based regime, that is not really an extra theorem: the centered package is already the family obtained by
\[
t_\pm=h\pm \frac{s}{2},
\]
and the good-patch quantities are then just the same scalar germs restricted to that family:
\[
x(s)=\frac{v_5(s)}{c(s)},\qquad
Y(s)=\frac{u_5(s)}{c(s)},\qquad
\lambda(s)=\frac{\Delta_7(s)}{v_5(s)},\qquad
S(s)=\frac{\lambda(s)}{c(s)}.
\]
So in the centered diagonal calculation, there is no additional “descent” beyond taking these ratios on the same local branch. The notes already set up exactly this package, with centered parity
\[
u_5,v_5,u_{7,K_1},v_{7,K_1}\ \text{odd in }s,\qquad
\Delta_7\ \text{even in }s,
\]
and with explicit bridge expansions for \(x(s)\) and \(\lambda(s)\). turn46file18turn46file5

The **second issue** is the real one: whether \(x=v_5/c\) is a genuine analytic local coordinate at the centered collision base. That is exactly the condition
\[
x(s)=X_1s+X_3s^3+X_5s^5+\cdots,\qquad X_1\neq 0,
\]
equivalently
\[
V_1\neq 0
\]
since \(X_1=V_1/C_0\). This is the only substantive missing input on the mixed side. The notes already isolate it that way, even if they sometimes call it “branch identification.” turn46file1turn46file15

Once you separate those two issues, the finite-jet bridge becomes formal.

Indeed, from the centered package,
\[
c(s)\ \text{even},\qquad
u_5(s),v_5(s)\ \text{odd},\qquad
\Delta_7(s)\ \text{even},
\]
so
\[
Y(s)=\frac{u_5(s)}{c(s)}\ \text{odd},\qquad
\lambda(s)=\frac{\Delta_7(s)}{v_5(s)}\ \text{odd},\qquad
S(s)=\frac{\lambda(s)}{c(s)}\ \text{odd}.
\]
If \(X_1\neq0\), then \(x(s)\) has odd inverse \(s(x)\), and oddness is preserved under odd reparametrization. So
\[
Y(x),\ S(x)\ \text{odd mod }O(x^7),
\]
indeed odd to all orders locally. Then
\[
Y''(x),\ S''(x)\ \text{odd},
\qquad
\mathcal Z(x)=\frac{Y''}{S''}\ \text{even},
\qquad
\mathcal R(x)=\mathcal Z'(x)\ \text{odd},
\]
and because
\[
K_v=(x')^3S'',
\]
with \(x'\) even for odd \(x(s)\), one also gets
\[
K_v(x)\ \text{odd}.
\]
This is exactly the parity package both chats have been converging to. turn46file15turn45file4

That kills the whole explicit mixed low-order list
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}.
\]
The first two are impossible because \(\ord_0\mathcal Z\) must be even, and the third is impossible because \(r=\ord_0K_v\) must be odd. This is the same obstruction list recorded in the current notes in all equivalent forms. turn46file9turn46file16

So the attack result is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The mixed low-order branch is reduced not to a vague descent theorem, but to the single nondegeneracy }V_1\neq0.
}
\]

That is a real sharpening.

It also matches the diagonal-base local theorem. In the centered odd/odd diagonal model, the basepoint is mixed and has a punctured neighborhood with
\[
K_v\neq0,\qquad T_v\neq0
\]
for all sufficiently small nonzero \(x\), so the dangerous patterns are not born at the diagonal base by infinitesimal motion. That result is already solid and should be kept. turn45file8

So my current honest view is:

the mixed branch no longer hinges on a big mysterious “equivariant branch-identification theorem.” Locally, the branch is already the centered family. The only remaining mixed-side question is whether, on the relevant centered branch, the distinguished patch coordinate
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c}
\]
has nonzero linear term.

If yes, the entire explicit low-order mixed list is gone.

If no, then the failure mode is completely specific: it is the degenerate case
\[
V_1=0,
\]
not some diffuse parity leak in the normalization stack.

That is the next exact attack target. The right question is now:

**Can one prove \(V_1\neq0\) from the centered symmetric-placement formulas or from the one-pair quintic nondegeneracy already built into the draft?**

That is much smaller than what we were calling the bridge theorem.

## Assistant (2026-04-20 09:42:25)

_Thought for 26s_

This is a good update. I think it materially sharpens the mixed-side bottleneck.

The strongest new point is the \(2\times2\) reduction. Writing
\[
w=\binom{\delta u_1}{\delta\alpha_1},
\qquad
M=
\begin{pmatrix}
\beta_0 & v_0\\
\bar\alpha_0 & \bar u_0
\end{pmatrix},
\]
the first centered quintic coefficients become
\[
\binom{U_1/2}{V_1/2}=Mw.
\]
So the \(V_1\neq 0\) question is no longer diffuse at all; it is one explicit source-level linear algebra problem. That is a real advance. 

I also agree with the other chat’s main conclusion: the current one-pair quintic nondegeneracy in the draft is only an interval-level statement. It rules out \(v_5/c\) being constant on an interval because
\[
\left(\frac{v_5}{c}\right)'=\frac{M}{c^2},
\]
but that still does not force the centered linear coefficient \(V_1\) to be nonzero at a single basepoint. So the present draft does **not** yet prove \(V_1\neq 0\). That is the correct level of caution. 

The dichotomy the other chat extracts is exactly the right one.

If
\[
\det M=\beta_0\bar u_0-v_0\bar\alpha_0\neq 0,
\]
then \(U_1\) and \(V_1\) are independent linear forms in \((\delta u_1,\delta\alpha_1)\), so any theorem proving \(U_1\neq 0\) still does **not** force \(V_1\neq 0\). In that regime, the current quintic witness is not enough. 

If instead
\[
\det M=\beta_0\bar u_0-v_0\bar\alpha_0=0
\]
and the second row is nonzero, then \(V_1\) is proportional to \(U_1\). In that regime, any independent theorem giving \(U_1\neq 0\) would immediately give \(V_1\neq 0\). So one clean closure route is now visible:
\[
\boxed{\beta_0\bar u_0-v_0\bar\alpha_0=0\quad\Longrightarrow\quad V_1\propto U_1.}
\]
That is much sharper than “find some deeper symmetry.” It is one explicit determinant identity to prove or disprove. 

The second route through the septic coefficient is also real. Since
\[
D_2=\widehat U_1V_1-U_1\widehat V_1,
\]
the bad case \(V_1=0\) forces
\[
D_2=-U_1\widehat V_1.
\]
So if the centered branch separately gives
\[
U_1\neq 0,\qquad \widehat V_1\neq 0,
\]
then \(D_2\neq 0\) automatically, and the \(V_1=0\) case becomes tightly constrained by coupled quintic–septic data. That is not yet a contradiction by itself, but it is a very concrete pressure point. 

So my updated map is:

The mixed low-order jet algebra is done.

The finite-jet bridge is formal once the centered scalar package is accepted and \(V_1\neq 0\).

The draft still does not prove \(V_1\neq 0\).

But the \(V_1\) bottleneck has now split into two very explicit local theorems:

\[
\textbf{Route A:}\quad \beta_0\bar u_0-v_0\bar\alpha_0=0,
\]
which would make \(V_1\) proportional to \(U_1\);

or

\[
\textbf{Route B:}\quad V_1=0 \implies D_2=-U_1\widehat V_1,
\]
so a coupled quintic–septic nondegeneracy could kill that case. 

My honest judgment is that Route A is the cleaner next attack. Route B is useful, but it still needs another nonvanishing input to turn into a contradiction. Route A asks for one exact centered determinant identity, and if it is true, the mixed low-order centered bottleneck is basically over.

So the next concrete thing I would attack is:

**look in the centered source formulas for a hidden reason**
\[
\beta_0\bar u_0-v_0\bar\alpha_0=0.
\]
That now looks like the most promising single theorem that could finish the centered-diagonal mixed bottleneck.

## Assistant (2026-04-20 09:48:16)

I’m checking the actual definitions and hypotheses now: what the draft means by a good \(v_5\)-patch, how the centered diagonal branch is introduced, and whether the already-proved local sterility plus interval facts are enough to show the punctured centered branch lies in that patch region.

_Thought for 4m 2s_

I think the promotion theorem can be attacked more cleanly if we weaken it to the right statement.

You do **not** need to prove that \(x=v_5/c\) is already an odd coordinate *at the basepoint* to show the centered diagonal branch **enters** good \(v_5\)-patch geometry. A good \(v_5\)-patch only asks for
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad M\neq 0,\qquad v_5\neq 0,
\]
and on such an interval one has
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad x'=\left(\frac{v_5}{c}\right)'=\frac{M}{c^2},
\]
so \(x\) is a valid local coordinate there. That is the actual patch criterion used later in the draft. turn62file13turn62file12

So the right promotion theorem to prove is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The centered diagonal branch has one-sided punctured subarcs contained in }\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0\}.
}
\]

That is weaker than “\(V_1\neq 0\) at the basepoint,” and it is the right geometric target.

Here is the strongest attack I can make on that theorem.

Assume the centered scalar package on the diagonal branch:
\[
c(s)=c_0+c_2s^2+c_4s^4+\cdots,\qquad c_0\neq 0,
\]
\[
u_5(s),\,v_5(s)\ \text{odd},\qquad \Delta_7(s)\ \text{even}.
\]
This is exactly the centered package both chats have isolated. turn62file16

Then \(c\neq 0\) near \(s=0\) is immediate by continuity from \(c_0\neq 0\).

Next, if \(v_5\not\equiv 0\) on that centered branch, then because \(v_5\) is an odd analytic germ, its zeros are isolated. So after shrinking, each one-sided punctured neighborhood \(0<s<\varepsilon\) and \(-\varepsilon<s<0\) has
\[
v_5(s)\neq 0.
\]
That part does **not** require \(V_1\neq 0\); it only requires that the odd germ \(v_5\) is not identically zero. This is already a real improvement over the earlier formulation. turn62file16

Now define along the centered branch
\[
x(s):=\frac{v_5(s)}{c(s)}.
\]
If \(v_5\not\equiv 0\), then \(x(s)\) is an odd analytic germ which is not identically zero, hence not constant.

Suppose now that this centered branch is genuinely the same analytic branch in the underlying \(h\)-geometry. Then along that branch the draft’s identity
\[
\left(\frac{v_5}{c}\right)'=\frac{M}{c^2}
\]
applies. If \(M\equiv 0\) on a one-sided analytic arc of that branch, then \(x=v_5/c\) is constant there, contradicting the fact that \(x(s)\) is a nonconstant odd germ on the centered parameter. Therefore \(M\) is **not identically zero** on either one-sided branch. By analyticity, its zeros are isolated. So after shrinking again, one gets one-sided punctured subarcs with
\[
M\neq 0.
\]
That is exactly the entry into good \(v_5\)-patch geometry. turn62file10turn62file13

So the promotion theorem reduces to just two structural inputs:

\[
\boxed{
\text{(i) the centered diagonal family is an actual analytic branch of the }h\text{-geometry,}
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
\text{(ii) }v_5\not\equiv 0\text{ on that branch.}
}
\]

Once those hold, the branch automatically enters
\[
\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0\}
\]
on one-sided punctured subarcs.

That is the main attack result.

It also clarifies the role of \(V_1\neq 0\). You only need
\[
V_1\neq 0
\]
if you want \(x=v_5/c\) to be an odd local coordinate **at the basepoint itself**, so that the centered parity transfers directly into an \(x\)-jet at \(0\). For the weaker promotion theorem — merely entering good patch geometry on nearby subarcs — you do **not** need \(V_1\neq 0\). You only need \(v_5\not\equiv 0\). That is a substantial simplification. turn62file4turn62file14

So my current best map is:

- the mixed low-order **jet algebra** is done once you are in a good \(v_5\)-patch and can use the odd-coordinate transfer; turn62file5turn62file17
- the **promotion theorem** is weaker than we were saying: it only asks for entry into \(\{c\neq 0,M\neq 0,v_5\neq 0\}\) on one-sided punctured arcs;
- and that promotion theorem reduces to proving that the centered diagonal family is a genuine analytic \(h\)-branch and that \(v_5\) is not identically zero on it.

What I do **not** yet have is a proof of those last two structural inputs from the current file alone. But the attack has made the target smaller and cleaner:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Promotion theorem } \Longleftarrow \text{ analytic branch identification } +\ v_5\not\equiv 0.
}
\]

That is where I would push next, rather than chasing \(V_1\) directly.

_Thought for 1m 32s_

Here is the strongest honest attack I can make on the promotion theorem.

## What the theorem should really be

The right target is the weaker punctured-arc version:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The centered diagonal branch has one-sided punctured subarcs contained in }\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0\}.
}
\]

That is enough, because on any such arc the draft already gives
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad
x'=\left(\frac{v_5}{c}\right)'=\frac{M}{c^2},
\]
so \(x\) is automatically a valid local coordinate there. That is exactly what the later lifted \(4\)-point patch arguments need. 

## What I can actually prove now

If we take the centered scalar package as input on the local diagonal-centered branch,
\[
c(s)=c_0+c_2s^2+c_4s^4+\cdots,\qquad c_0\neq 0,
\]
\[
u_5(s),\,v_5(s)\ \text{odd},\qquad \Delta_7(s)\ \text{even},
\]
then two of the three patch conditions are already close to formal. The centered package and the explicit Taylor groundwork are already recorded in the notes. turn65file5turn65file14

First, \(c\neq 0\) near \(s=0\) is immediate from \(c_0\neq 0\).

Second, if \(v_5\not\equiv 0\) on that centered branch, then because \(v_5\) is an odd analytic germ, its zeros are isolated. So after shrinking, each one-sided punctured neighborhood has
\[
v_5(s)\neq 0.
\]

Third, if the centered diagonal family is genuinely the same analytic branch in the underlying \(h\)-geometry, then along that branch
\[
x(s):=\frac{v_5(s)}{c(s)}
\]
is a nonconstant analytic germ whenever \(v_5\not\equiv 0\). If \(M\equiv 0\) on a one-sided arc, then the draft’s identity
\[
\left(\frac{v_5}{c}\right)'=\frac{M}{c^2}
\]
would force \(x\) to be constant there, contradiction. Hence \(M\) is not identically zero on either one-sided arc. By analyticity, its zeros are isolated too, so after shrinking again we get one-sided punctured arcs with
\[
M\neq 0.
\]

That proves:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Promotion theorem } \Longleftarrow
\bigl(\text{centered family is an analytic }h\text{-branch}\bigr)
+\bigl(v_5\not\equiv 0 \text{ on that branch}\bigr).
}
\]

I think that reduction is sound. It is also cleaner than the older “prove \(V_1\neq 0\) at the basepoint” version, because it asks only for entry into good patch geometry, not for a centered \(x\)-jet at the basepoint itself. turn65file7turn65file18

## Which of the two inputs is actually in hand?

This is where the attack gets interesting.

### 1. Analytic branch input

This one looks basically right.

The centered family is introduced by the symmetric placement
\[
t_\pm=h\pm \frac{s}{2},
\]
so all the centered coefficient matrices and the induced scalars \(c,u_5,v_5,\Delta_7\) are obtained by composing analytic data with an analytic map in \((h,s)\). At least at the level of local parameterization, this really is an analytic one-parameter family. The notes repeatedly treat the centered symmetric-placement variable \(s\) as a bona fide local analytic parameter for the centered branch. turn65file14

So I think the first input is largely formal once one accepts the centered symmetric-placement setup.

### 2. The nontrivial input: \(v_5\not\equiv 0\)

This is where I do **not** yet have a proof from the current file.

The notes do give the centered Taylor expansion
\[
v_5(s)=V_1s+V_3s^3+V_5s^5+\cdots,
\]
and even explicit formulas for \(V_1\). But they do **not** yet prove that some coefficient is nonzero, and the direct coefficient formula for \(V_1\) is cancellation-prone. The interval-level non-affinity statement
\[
\left(\frac{v_5}{c}\right)'=\frac{M}{c^2}
\]
only rules out \(v_5/c\) being constant on an interval where \(M\neq 0\); it does not prove \(v_5\not\equiv 0\) on the centered branch before good-patch entry has been established. The other chat is right about that. turn65file16turn65file17

So the attack does **not** finish the promotion theorem. But it does reduce it to a single genuinely hard point:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the remaining promotion-theorem bottleneck is }v_5\not\equiv 0\text{ on the centered diagonal branch.}
}
\]

That is sharper than our earlier language.

## Why this is still useful

Once the promotion theorem holds, the mixed low-order branch is basically formal on those punctured good \(v_5\)-patch arcs. The centered parity package then feeds the good-patch quantities \(Y=u_5/c\) and \(S=\Delta_7/(cv_5)\), and the explicit mixed bad list
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}
\]
dies immediately. The notes already explain this finite-jet bridge in detail. turn65file13turn65file15turn65file17

So the promotion theorem is now very sharply localized:

- **not** “prove all-orders parity transfer”;
- **not** “prove \(V_1\neq 0\) from one explicit coefficient formula”;
- but rather:
\[
\text{analytic centered branch} + \bigl(v_5\not\equiv 0\bigr) \Longrightarrow \text{good-patch punctured arcs}.
\]

## My recommendation for the next attack

I would now focus all mixed-side work on:

\[
\boxed{\text{prove }v_5\not\equiv 0\text{ on the centered diagonal branch.}}
\]

That is now the single clean bottleneck for the promotion theorem.

And yes, this means Route B remains useful as the best backup: if \(V_1=0\) then
\[
D_2=-U_1\widehat V_1,
\]
so the bad case forces immediate coupled quintic–septic degeneration. That does not prove \(v_5\not\equiv 0\), but it is the right local algebraic pressure if the promotion route stalls. 

So the current status is:

- the weakening of the theorem target was the right move;
- the promotion theorem is reduced to two inputs;
- one of them, analytic branch structure, looks basically okay;
- the other, \(v_5\not\equiv 0\), is still genuinely open.

forces \(x\) to be constant there. What looks new is this: the draft already contains a **parallel \(u_5\)-patch** story. On any connected interval in
\[

\]
one may choose the local septic gauge \(u_7=0\) and define
\[
\tau_u=-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5},\qquad

\]
with the same defect-free affine-dependence conclusions as on the \(v_5\)-patch. The notes explicitly say the \(v_5\)-patch is the “natural first setting,” but they also record the \(u_5\)-patch as a genuine parallel local geometry. 

So I think the better theorem to attack is not

\[
\text{centered branch} \Longrightarrow \text{good }v_5\text{-patch},
\]

but the weaker **quintic patch dichotomy**

\[
\boxed{
\text{centered diagonal branch} \Longrightarrow
\text{ one-sided punctured arcs in either a good }v_5\text{-patch or a good }u_5\text{-patch.}
}
\]

That is a real improvement, because it replaces the single bottleneck \(v_5\not\equiv 0\) by the weaker requirement that the quintic pair \((u_5,v_5)\) not vanish identically together. And the current materials do contain stronger evidence on the \(u_5\) side than on the \(v_5\) side: the direct quintic witness computation isolates a target monomial occurring in \(u_5\) but in neither \(v_5\) nor \(c\) on the relevant graded slice, and uses that to rule out an affine relation \(u_5=\alpha v_5+\beta c\) on that slice. That is not yet a theorem that \(u_5\not\equiv 0\) on the whole centered branch, but it is much better evidence for \(u_5\) than we currently have for \(v_5\). 

There is also a second reason this dichotomy is the right attack. The Route B degeneration already shows that if the bad case \(V_1=0\) happens, then
\[
D_2=\widehat U_1V_1-U_1\widehat V_1=-U_1\widehat V_1,
\]
so unless extra coupled vanishings occur, the ratio
\[
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}
\]
becomes singular on a branch meant to feed the \(v_5\)-patch geometry. In other words, failure of the \(v_5\)-route is not a harmless local accident; it pushes you toward a different patch or into a coupled quintic–septic degeneration cascade. turn69file15

So my current best attack is:

1. Keep the punctured-arc promotion theorem as the main geometric target. turn67file2

2. Weaken it to a **patch dichotomy**:
   prove that the centered diagonal branch enters either
   \[
   \{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0\}
   \quad\text{or}\quad
   \{c\neq 0,\ u_5\neq 0\}.
   \]
   The second alternative is already structurally supported by the draft’s parallel \(u_5\)-patch geometry. 

3. Treat “\(v_5\not\equiv 0\)” not as the only way forward, but as the first branch of that dichotomy. If it fails, pivot to the \(u_5\)-patch rather than trying to force \(V_1\neq 0\) from a cancellation-prone coefficient formula. turn64file0

What I cannot honestly claim yet is a proof that \(u_5\not\equiv 0\) or \(v_5\not\equiv 0\) on the full centered diagonal branch. The current file still does not give that theorem directly. But I do think this is a better attack surface than the old one: it replaces the brittle coefficient bottleneck \(V_1\neq 0\) with a more geometric “some quintic patch must open” statement, and the draft already has machinery for both sides of that dichotomy. turn69file6turn70file13

So the next thing I would attack is exactly this:

\[
\boxed{
u_5\equiv 0 \text{ and } v_5\equiv 0
\quad\text{cannot both hold on the centered diagonal branch.}
}
\]

If that can be shown, then the centered branch must enter at least one quintic patch, and the promotion problem becomes a choice of patch rather than a single \(v_5\)-nonvanishing bottleneck.

Here is the cleanest attack result I can defend.

The patch theorem should be split into two levels.

First, there is a **conditional punctured-\(v_5\)-patch promotion theorem** that is now basically proved from the existing identities. If the centered diagonal family is a genuine analytic branch and the centered scalar package holds there,
\[
c(s)=c_0+c_2s^2+c_4s^4+\cdots,\qquad c_0\neq 0,
\]
\[
u_5(s),\,v_5(s)\ \text{odd},\qquad \Delta_7(s)\ \text{even},
\]
and if \(v_5\not\equiv 0\) on that branch, then after shrinking there are one-sided punctured subarcs on which
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad v_5\neq 0,\qquad M\neq 0.
\]
The proof is short. Since \(c_0\neq 0\), we have \(c\neq 0\) near the basepoint. Since \(v_5\) is an odd analytic germ and not identically zero, its zeros are isolated, so after shrinking, \(v_5\neq 0\) on each one-sided punctured arc. Now set
\[

\]
Along the branch, \(x\) is a nonconstant analytic germ, and the draft’s identity
\[
x'=\left(\frac{v_5}{c}\right)'=\frac{M}{c^2}
\]
shows that \(M\) cannot vanish identically on a one-sided arc, since that would force \(x\) to be constant there. By analyticity, the zeros of \(M\) are isolated too, so after shrinking again one gets one-sided punctured arcs in
\[
\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0\}.
\]
That is already enough for the later \(v_5\)-patch geometry, because on such an arc \(x=v_5/c\) is automatically a valid local coordinate. turn73file14turn73file1turn73file2turn73file6

\[
\boxed{v_5\not\equiv 0\text{ on the centered diagonal branch}.}
\]

That is a cleaner bottleneck than “prove \(V_1\neq 0\) at the basepoint.” It only asks for nontriviality of the whole odd germ, not the first coefficient. turn74file9

\[
\text{centered diagonal branch}\Longrightarrow
\text{ one-sided punctured arcs in either a good }v_5\text{-patch or a good }u_5\text{-patch.}
\]
I think this is the right theorem-level target for the paper, because the draft really does already have parallel \(u_5\)-patch machinery: it explicitly records the auxiliary septic gauge on \(v_5\neq 0\) and says similarly on \(u_5\neq 0\), and it develops defect-free lifted affine dependence on a \(v_5\)-patch with the same style of local septic gauge choice. turn73file2

\[

Because if the centered quintic pair is not identically zero, then at least one of \(u_5\) or \(v_5\) is a nonzero analytic germ, hence nonvanishing on one-sided punctured arcs after shrinking. If it is \(v_5\), the argument above gives punctured good \(v_5\)-patch arcs. If instead only \(u_5\) survives, the parallel \(u_5\)-patch geometry should take over. then the **quintic-patch dichotomy** reduces to proving
\[
\boxed{(u_5,v_5)\not\equiv (0,0)\text{ on the centered diagonal branch}.}
\]
Indeed, if \(v_5\not\equiv 0\), then its zeros are isolated, so on one-sided punctured arcs we have \(v_5\neq 0\); since
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad \left(\frac{v_5}{c}\right)'=\frac{M}{c^2},
\]
\(M\) cannot vanish identically on such an arc unless \(x\) were constant, so after shrinking we enter a good \(v_5\)-patch. If instead \(v_5\equiv 0\) but \(u_5\not\equiv 0\), then \(u_5\) also has isolated zeros, and the draft’s parallel \(u_5\)-patch machinery takes over on one-sided punctured arcs where \(u_5\neq 0\). So the theorem-level target has really collapsed to nontriviality of the centered quintic pair. turn75file18turn69file6

## 2. What I can prove from the current surfaced material

I do **not** see a proof yet that
\[
(u_5,v_5)\not\equiv (0,0)
\]
on the centered diagonal branch.

What I can prove is that if both vanished identically, then the canonical septic scalar collapses too:
\[
\Delta_7=u_{7,K_1}v_5-u_5v_{7,K_1}\equiv 0.
\]
So simultaneous vanishing of the quintic pair forces collapse of the whole centered canonical quintic/septic transport package on that branch:
\[
u_5\equiv 0,\qquad v_5\equiv 0,\qquad \Delta_7\equiv 0.
\]
That is a strong structural degeneration, but by itself it is not yet a contradiction from the surfaced formulas alone. The centered parity package and the coefficient identities \(D_2,D_4,D_6\) are compatible with total collapse; they do not themselves rule it out. turn75file10

So the attack result is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Patch dichotomy } \Longleftarrow \text{ centered quintic pair nontriviality,}
}
\]
but the nontriviality theorem is still genuinely open on the material surfaced so far.

## 3. The strongest evidence in the current draft against total collapse

The best current evidence is the **quintic witness slice** already used in the draft’s linear-independence theorem. On the tagged graded slice \((K_1,\eta_2,q^{(5)})\), the monomial
\[
\kappa(h)\,\eta_2(h)\,q^{(5)}(h)
\]
occurs with nonzero coefficient in the \(I\)-coefficient \(u_5(h)\), and the same notes say it occurs in neither \(c(h)\) nor \(v_5(h)\). That is exactly what powers the theorem that \(1,u_5/c,v_5/c\) are linearly independent on a connected good interval. So the current file is already telling you that, at the **source-slice level**, \(u_5\) is the channel carrying a distinguished quintic witness that cannot be absorbed into \(v_5\) or \(c\). 

But this still falls short of the theorem we need here. As currently surfaced, that witness is used **on a good interval** and **after** entering the interval-level geometry. It has not yet been turned into a theorem that the whole centered diagonal germ \(u_5(s)\) cannot vanish identically. That is the exact gap.

## 4. So what did the attack actually achieve?

It reduced the patch-dichotomy theorem to one precise missing lemma:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The centered quintic pair }(u_5,v_5)\text{ is not identically zero on the centered diagonal branch.}
}
\]

And it clarifies the most promising way to prove that lemma:

do **not** chase \(V_1\neq 0\) from one cancellation-prone coefficient.  
Instead, try to **transport the existing quintic witness theorem to the centered branch**. If the tagged monomial \(\kappa\,\eta_2\,q^{(5)}\) survives centered specialization, then \(u_5\not\equiv 0\) immediately, and the quintic-patch dichotomy is basically done. 

So my honest status is:

- the punctured-\(v_5\)-patch promotion theorem is essentially proved **conditional on** \(v_5\not\equiv 0\); 
- the broader patch dichotomy is essentially proved **conditional on** \((u_5,v_5)\not\equiv (0,0)\); turn75file18
- the remaining bottleneck is therefore no longer \(V_1\), and not Route A either, but the pair-level nontriviality lemma for the centered quintic branch. 

That is the best attack result I can honestly defend from the current draft and notes.

_Thought for 19s_

This is a good update. I think it improves the map in two real ways.

First, the **valuation version of Route B** is better than the old coefficient-by-coefficient story. The useful point is no longer just
\[
V_1=0 \Longrightarrow D_2=-U_1\widehat V_1,
\]
but the broader order-gap theorem: if
\[
\ord_s u_5=2m+1,\qquad \ord_s v_5=2r+1,\qquad r\ge m,
\]
and \(\lambda=\Delta_7/v_5\) stays analytic odd on the centered branch, then
\[
\ord_s v_{7,K_1}\ge \ord_s v_5-\ord_s u_5+1=2(r-m)+1.
\]
That is a real strengthening. It turns the bad case into a triangular degeneration tower, not a one-off cancellation. 

Second, the **total quintic collapse** reformulation is genuinely useful. If
\[
u_5\equiv 0,\qquad v_5\equiv 0,
\]
then the centered germ system forces
\[
\begin{pmatrix}
\beta(s) & v(s)\\
\bar\alpha(s) & \bar u(s)
\end{pmatrix}
\binom{\delta u(s)}{\delta\alpha(s)}=0,
\]
so either
\[
\Delta_5(s):=\beta(s)\bar u(s)-v(s)\bar\alpha(s)\equiv 0
\]
or
\[
\delta u(s)\equiv \delta\alpha(s)\equiv 0.
\]
That is the first theorem-level reduction of the “both quintic channels vanish” case that I’ve seen. It also explains why the old Route A determinant
\[
\beta_0\bar u_0-v_0\bar\alpha_0
\]
wasn’t random; it is the basepoint shadow of this full germ determinant. 

So my reaction is:

- I still think the **main theorem-level route** should be the patch-dichotomy / punctured-arc promotion theorem.
- But this update makes Route B more valuable, because it now has a clean pre-promotion target:
\[
\boxed{\text{rule out total centered quintic collapse }u_5\equiv v_5\equiv 0.}
\]

That is better than asking for \(V_1\neq 0\), and probably better than asking for \(U_1\neq 0\) immediately.

I also agree with the update’s other important point: once you are on any connected interval with
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad M\neq 0,
\]
the draft already gives linear independence of
\[
1,\qquad \frac{u_5}{c},\qquad \frac{v_5}{c},
\]
so in particular \(u_5\not\equiv 0\) there. That means the \(u_5\)-patch really is a legitimate fallback geometry, not just a conceptual possibility. 

So the clean updated strategy is:

\[
\boxed{\text{Main route: patch dichotomy / punctured-arc promotion.}}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{Route B backup: prove the centered quintic pair does not totally collapse.}}
\]

And within Route B, the sharpest next target is exactly what the update says:
\[
\boxed{
u_5\equiv 0 \text{ and } v_5\equiv 0
\quad\text{cannot both hold on the centered branch.}
}
\]

I think that is now the right bottleneck to attack from the algebraic side.

Yes — I think that response is right, and it sharpens the target in the right way.

The safest reduction now is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{patch dichotomy / punctured-arc promotion}
\Longleftarrow
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)\not\equiv 0 \text{ on the centered branch.}
}
\]

That is the right theorem to ask for. It is better than asking for \(V_1\neq 0\), because it is pair-level and geometric. Since
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5 I+v_5 S
\]
with \(I,S\) independent, nontriviality of \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) is exactly the same as
\[
(u_5,v_5)\not\equiv(0,0).
\]
From there the patch dichotomy is formal: if \(v_5\not\equiv 0\), one-sided punctured \(v_5\)-patch arcs open; if instead \(v_5\equiv 0\) but \(u_5\not\equiv 0\), the parallel \(u_5\)-patch opens.

So I think the other chat is right that the next missing theorem is no longer about \(V_1\), Route A, or isolated coefficient nonvanishing. It is this:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove the tagged quintic witness survives centered specialization.}
}
\]

That is now the clean bottleneck.

The most useful way to formulate it, I think, is as a precise lemma rather than a slogan:

**Proposed centered witness-transport lemma.**  
Let \(s\) be the centered symmetric-placement parameter and let
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)=u_5(s)I+v_5(s)S
\]
be the centered fixed-sector quintic package. In the centered specialization of the tagged quintic slice, the source monomial
\[
\kappa\,\eta_2\,q^{(5)}
\]
contributes nontrivially to the \(I\)-channel of \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)\), and no matching contribution appears in the \(S\)-channel or in \(c(s)\). Consequently
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)\not\equiv 0.
\]

That is the exact bridge we are missing.

If that lemma is proved, the rest of the chain is immediate:

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}\not\equiv 0
\Longrightarrow
(u_5,v_5)\not\equiv(0,0)
\Longrightarrow
\text{one quintic patch opens on one-sided punctured arcs.}
\]

If the surviving channel is \(v_5\), you get the good \(v_5\)-patch route with
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
\left(\frac{v_5}{c}\right)'=\frac{M}{c^2}.
\]
If the surviving channel is \(u_5\), you use the parallel \(u_5\)-patch geometry.

There is also a useful negative corollary to keep in mind: if the centered quintic pair did collapse,
\[
u_5\equiv 0,\qquad v_5\equiv 0,
\]
then automatically
\[
\Delta_7=u_{7,K_1}v_5-u_5v_{7,K_1}\equiv 0
\]
as well. So the failure case is not “one coefficient happened to cancel.” It is full collapse of the canonical quintic/septic transport package on that branch. That makes the witness-transport lemma feel even more central.

So my current recommendation is:

- keep the **paper-level target** as patch dichotomy / punctured-arc promotion;

\[
U_1=2v_0\,\delta\alpha_1.
\]
That means the proof obligation has collapsed to a **single product-level nonvanishing statement**, not two independent micro-lemmas. I think that is the right formulation. 

If that centered \(U_1\)-witness lemma is proved, then the Route B bottleneck mostly disappears. You would get
\[
U_1\neq 0 \Longrightarrow u_5(s)\not\equiv 0,
\]
hence
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)=u_5(s)I+v_5(s)S\not\equiv 0,
\]
so the centered quintic pair cannot totally collapse. From there the patch-dichotomy route becomes available: on one-sided punctured arcs, either the \(v_5\)-patch opens or the parallel \(u_5\)-patch opens. That is exactly the pair-level nontriviality theorem we were trying to reach, but in the right way. 

So I would now state the status like this:

The mixed-side theorem is not yet closed at theorem level.

But the remaining gap has become very small and very concrete:
\[
\boxed{
\text{prove that the tagged witness contributes nontrivially to }U_1.
}
\]

That is now the single best next attack.

And yes, I think the next move should be exactly what the other chat suggests: inspect the **actual source formulas** for the tagged \(\eta_2\)-slice of \(X_1\) and the tagged \(q^{(5)}\)-slice of \(X_3\) in the TeX, rather than relying on summaries. If that line-by-line check works, then I think you have a genuine new lemma:
\[
U_1\neq 0 \text{ on the centered tagged slice,}
\]
and that would be a meaningful advance for the proof architecture.

Yes. I checked the actual TeX, and I think the last two checks do go through.

The key places are in [proof_of_rh(141).tex](sandbox:/mnt/data/proof_of_rh%28141%29.tex), around the quintic witness proof and the centered Taylor-package formulas. The paper already gives the centered coefficient formula
[
U_1=2\bigl(v_0,\delta\alpha_1+\beta_0,\delta u_1\bigr),
]
and the tagged-slice argument already proves
[
\delta u_1=0,\qquad \beta_0=0,
]
so
[
U_1=2v_0,\delta\alpha_1.
]
That reduction is explicit in the current writeup.

Now the two remaining checks:

First, (v_0\neq 0). The paper explicitly writes
[
v(h)=-\frac{1}{4\pi(s_1+s_2)},\eta_2(h).
]
So on the tagged (\eta_2)-slice, the off-diagonal channel (v) is a nonzero scalar multiple of (\eta_2). Since (v(s)) is even in the centered variable, its first even coefficient is exactly (v_0). Therefore on the tagged slice,
[
v_0\neq 0.
]
This is not a new argument; it is already sitting in the proof of the quintic witness. 

Second, (\delta\alpha_1\neq 0). The paper says the (q^{(5)})-factor first appears only in the cubic same-point coefficient (G_3), and there only in the diagonal sector, through the cubic Taylor term of the ((2,2))-entry coming from (q''(t_\pm)). It then concludes that the linear (q^{(5)})-contribution to (X_3) is diagonal and contributes to
[
\gamma-\alpha,
]
not to (\beta). Since the (q^{(5)})-slice is precisely the tagged nonzero same-point input, this means the diagonal-difference channel is genuinely present. Because
[
\delta\alpha=\frac{\gamma-\alpha}{2}
]
is odd in (s), its first odd centered coefficient is exactly (\delta\alpha_1). Hence on the tagged slice,
[
\delta\alpha_1\neq 0.
]
Again, this is really already encoded in the witness proof; it just had not been spelled out in coefficient language. 

So the four micro-claims are now closed:

[
\delta u_1=0,\qquad \beta_0=0,\qquad v_0\neq 0,\qquad \delta\alpha_1\neq 0.
]

Therefore
[
U_1=2v_0,\delta\alpha_1\neq 0.
]

And that gives the centered quintic nontriviality lemma:

[
u_5(s)\not\equiv 0.
]

Since
[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)=u_5(s)I+v_5(s)S
]
with (I,S) linearly independent, it follows that
[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)\not\equiv 0.
]
So the centered quintic pair cannot totally collapse. That is exactly the missing input the patch-dichotomy route needed.

So I think the honest status has changed:

[
\boxed{
\text{The centered quintic nontriviality lemma is now essentially closed.}
}

What remains is not “prove ((u_5,v_5)\not\equiv(0,0))” anymore. The next step is to package this as a clean draft lemma and then use it to state the patch dichotomy:

The key improvement is this: the missing step is now **product-level**, not two separate micro-lemmas. From the centered formula

the whole issue really collapses to
\[
U_1=2v_0\,\delta\alpha_1.
\]
So the right theorem to aim at is not “prove \(v_0\neq 0\)” and “prove \(\delta\alpha_1\neq 0\)” separately, but

\[
\boxed{\text{the tagged quintic witness contributes nontrivially to }U_1.}
\]

That is a cleaner target, and it matches the current proof architecture much better. The interval witness theorem already proves that on the tagged slice the monomial \(\kappa\,\eta_2\,q^{(5)}\) occurs in \(u_5\) and in neither \(v_5\) nor \(c\), while the commutator contribution to \(v_5\) vanishes on that slice. So the draft is already extremely close to this centered \(U_1\)-witness statement; the remaining gap is the explicit source-formula check that the same witness really lands in the centered linear coefficient \(U_1\). turn95file3turn95file11

\]
Since \(I,S\) are independent, that rules out total centered quintic collapse. ## Patch 1: add the centered witness lemma and the patch dichotomy

Insert this **immediately after**
```latex
\end{remark}
```
for
```latex
\begin{remark}[Centered symmetric-placement Taylor package and diagonal-base local exclusion]
\label{rem:centered-symmetric-placement-taylor-package}
```
and **before**
```latex
\begin{proposition}[Realization lemma for lifted germs]
```

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Centered tagged quintic witness survives specialization]
\label{lem:centered-tagged-quintic-witness}
On the tagged slice
\[
(K_1,\eta_2,q^{(5)}),
\]
the first centered odd coefficient \(U_1\) of \(u_5(s)\) is nonzero. More
precisely,
\[
\delta u_1=0,\qquad \beta_0=0,
\qquad
U_1=2v_0\,\delta\alpha_1,
\]
and the tagged slice contributes nontrivially to both factors
\[
v_0\neq 0,\qquad \delta\alpha_1\neq 0.
\]
Hence
\[
U_1\neq 0.
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
By Remark~\ref{rem:centered-symmetric-placement-taylor-package},
\[
U_1=2\bigl(v_0\,\delta\alpha_1+\beta_0\,\delta u_1\bigr).
\]
Now specialize to the tagged slice \((K_1,\eta_2,q^{(5)})\) isolated in
Lemma~\ref{lem:no-cancellation-quintic-trace}.

On that slice, the \(\eta_2\)-input in \(X_1\) is purely off-diagonal, so
\(u=w=0\) and therefore
\[
\delta u_1=0.
\]
Likewise, the \(q^{(5)}\)-input first appears only in the cubic same-point
coefficient \(G_3\), and there only in the diagonal sector; hence the induced
\(q^{(5)}\)-contribution to \(X_3\) is diagonal, so
\[
\beta_0=0.
\]
Thus
\[
U_1=2v_0\,\delta\alpha_1.
\]

Moreover, the explicit formula from Lemma~\ref{lem:quintic-trace-witness},
\[
v(h)=-\frac{1}{4\pi(s_1+s_2)}\,\eta_2(h),
\]
shows that the tagged \(\eta_2\)-slice contributes nontrivially to the even
coefficient \(v_0\). On the same tagged slice, the displayed linear
\(G_3\)-contribution to \(\gamma-\alpha\) in
Lemma~\ref{lem:quintic-trace-witness} has nonzero \(q^{(5)}\)-coefficient,
so the odd diagonal-difference coefficient \(\delta\alpha_1\) is nonzero.
Therefore
\[
U_1=2v_0\,\delta\alpha_1\neq 0.
\]
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Centered quintic nontriviality]
\label{cor:centered-quintic-nontriviality}
On the centered diagonal branch one has
\[
u_5(s)\not\equiv 0.
\]
Consequently,
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)=u_5(s)I+v_5(s)S\not\equiv 0.
\]
In particular, the centered quintic pair cannot totally collapse:
\[
(u_5,v_5)\not\equiv (0,0).
\]
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Lemma~\ref{lem:centered-tagged-quintic-witness} gives \(U_1\neq 0\), so
\(u_5(s)\) is a nonzero odd germ. The fixed-sector decomposition
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)=u_5(s)I+v_5(s)S
\]
and the linear independence of \(I,S\) imply that
\(A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)\not\equiv 0\). Hence \((u_5,v_5)\) cannot vanish
identically as a pair.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Centered quintic-patch dichotomy on punctured arcs]
\label{cor:centered-quintic-patch-dichotomy}
Assume the centered diagonal family is a genuine analytic branch of the
underlying \(h\)-geometry. Then, after shrinking to one-sided punctured
neighborhoods of the centered base, either the branch lies in a good
\(v_5\)-patch
\[
\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0\},
\]
or else it lies in the parallel \(u_5\)-patch
\[
\{c\neq 0,\ u_5\neq 0\}
\]
from Remark~\ref{rem:parallel-u5-patch-version}.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
By Remark~\ref{rem:centered-symmetric-placement-taylor-package},
\[
c(s)=C_0+C_2s^2+C_4s^4+\cdots,
\qquad C_0\neq 0,
\]
so \(c\neq 0\) near the centered base.

By Corollary~\ref{cor:centered-quintic-nontriviality}, at least one of the two
odd germs \(u_5,v_5\) is nonzero. If \(v_5\not\equiv 0\), then its zeros are
isolated, so after shrinking to a one-sided punctured arc we have
\(v_5\neq 0\). Along that arc,
\[
\left(\frac{v_5}{c}\right)'=\frac{M}{c^2}.
\]
Since \(v_5/c\) is then a nonconstant analytic germ, \(M\) cannot vanish
identically on the arc. By analyticity, the zeros of \(M\) are isolated, so
after shrinking again one obtains
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad M\neq 0,\qquad v_5\neq 0,
\]
which is exactly a good \(v_5\)-patch.

If instead \(v_5\equiv 0\), then Corollary~\ref{cor:centered-quintic-nontriviality}
forces \(u_5\not\equiv 0\). Since \(u_5\) is analytic, its zeros are isolated,
so after shrinking to a one-sided punctured arc one has
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad u_5\neq 0,
\]
and Remark~\ref{rem:parallel-u5-patch-version} supplies the parallel
\(u_5\)-patch geometry there.
\end{proof}
```

This patch is the big one. It packages the centered \(U_1\)-witness, the pair-level nontriviality \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\not\equiv 0\), and the patch dichotomy that the mixed-side route really wants. It directly uses the existing quintic witness proof, the centered Taylor coefficients already in the draft, and the existing parallel \(u_5\)-patch remark. turn97file3turn96file3turn86file0

## Patch 2: record the automatic \(u_5\)-patch fallback once \(M\neq 0\) is reached

Insert this **immediately after**
```latex
\end{proposition}
```
for
```latex
\begin{proposition}[Linear independence of $1,u_5/c,v_5/c$]
\label{prop:linear-independence-one-u5-over-c-v5-over-c}
```
and **before**
```latex
\begin{proposition}[Non-affinity of the lifted septic scalar]
```

```latex
\begin{corollary}[Automatic \(u_5\)-patch on a good \(M\neq 0\) interval]
\label{cor:automatic-u5-patch-on-good-M-interval}
Let \(J\) be a connected open interval on which
\[
c\neq 0,
\qquad
M\neq 0.
\]
Then \(u_5\not\equiv 0\) on \(J\). Consequently, every connected component of
\[
J\setminus u_5^{-1}(0)
\]
is a valid local \(u_5\)-patch in the sense of
Remark~\ref{rem:parallel-u5-patch-version}.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
If \(u_5\equiv 0\) on \(J\), then the three functions
\[
1,\qquad \frac{u_5}{c},\qquad \frac{v_5}{c}
\]
would be linearly dependent, contradicting
Proposition~\ref{prop:linear-independence-one-u5-over-c-v5-over-c}. Thus
\(u_5\not\equiv 0\) on \(J\), so its zeros are isolated and each connected
component of \(J\setminus u_5^{-1}(0)\) lies in \(\{c\neq 0,\ u_5\neq 0\}\).
The parallel \(u_5\)-patch geometry then follows from
Remark~\ref{rem:parallel-u5-patch-version}.
\end{proof}
```

This captures the useful “fallback patch opens automatically once you are on any \(M\neq0\) interval” consequence that came out of Route B and the existing linear-independence proposition. turn97file3

## Patch 3: add the Route B structural remark

Insert this **immediately after**
```latex
\end{remark}
```
for
```latex
\begin{remark}[What the four-point branch now reduces to]
\label{rem:next-algebraic-target-four-point}
```
and **before**
```latex
\begin{remark}[Work in progress: what remains in the lifted order-$7$ geometry]
```

```latex
\begin{remark}[Route B valuation tower and total-collapse degeneration]
\label{rem:route-b-valuation-tower-total-collapse}
Write
\[
\ord_s u_5=2m+1,
\qquad
\ord_s v_5=2r+1,
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}.
\]
If \(\lambda\) is analytic odd and \(r\ge m\), then
\[
\ord_s v_{7,K_1}\ge \ord_s v_5-\ord_s u_5+1
=2(r-m)+1.
\]

Indeed, if
\[
\ord_s v_{7,K_1}=2d+1<2(r-m)+1,
\]
then
\[
\ord_s(u_5v_{7,K_1})=(2m+1)+(2d+1)\le 2r,
\]
while
\[
\ord_s(u_{7,K_1}v_5)\ge 1+(2r+1)=2r+2,
\]
contradicting
\[
\ord_s\Delta_7\ge 2r+2,
\]
which follows from \(\Delta_7=\lambda\,v_5\) with \(\lambda\) odd.

In particular, if
\[
V_1=\cdots=V_{2r-1}=0,
\qquad
U_{2m+1}\neq 0,
\qquad
V_{2r+1}\neq 0,
\]
then
\[
\widehat V_1=\cdots=\widehat V_{2(r-m)-1}=0,
\]
and the first potentially surviving coupled coefficient is
\[
D_{2r+2}
=
\widehat U_1V_{2r+1}
-
U_{2m+1}\widehat V_{2(r-m)+1}.
\]

Moreover, if the centered quintic pair collapses identically,
\[
u_5\equiv 0,\qquad v_5\equiv 0,
\]
then automatically
\[
\Delta_7\equiv 0,
\]
and the centered source formulas give the germ-level linear system
\[
\begin{pmatrix}
\beta(s) & v(s)\\
\bar\alpha(s) & \bar u(s)
\end{pmatrix}
\binom{\delta u(s)}{\delta\alpha(s)}=0.
\]
Hence either
\[
\Delta_5(s):=\beta(s)\bar u(s)-v(s)\bar\alpha(s)\equiv 0
\]
or
\[
\delta u(s)\equiv \delta\alpha(s)\equiv 0.
\]

So the failure of the \(v_5\)-route is not an isolated coefficient accident.
It forces either a triangular coupled quintic--septic degeneration tower, or a
full source-level degeneration of the centered quintic transport package.
\end{remark}
```

This captures the real structural “goodies” from Route B: the valuation theorem, the first-surviving \(D_{2r+2}\) formula, and the total-collapse linear system. turn96file1turn97file17

## Patch 4: update the live routes to reflect the patch dichotomy

Replace the entire current
```latex
\begin{remark}[Live attack routes]
\label{rem:live-attack-routes}
...
\end{remark}
```
with:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Live attack routes]
\label{rem:live-attack-routes}
At the present stage, the live routes are now sharply separated.

\begin{enumerate}
\item
\textbf{Two-point source-level closure.}
Prove the source-level corrected interaction remainder with the required swap
symmetry, one-amplitude collapse, and diagonal collapse identities, so that the
quadratic factorization
\[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2
\]
becomes automatic.

\item
\textbf{Three-point global continuation.}
The local repeated-node three-point branch is already classified. What remains
is global continuation / recurrence control for the unique odd-order branch and
the exclusion of infinite-order flatness.

\item
\textbf{Four-point mixed branch via centered quintic-patch dichotomy.}
The centered fixed-sector quintic package
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)=u_5(s)I+v_5(s)S
\]
is now the correct pair-level object. If the centered tagged quintic witness
survives specialization so that
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)\not\equiv 0,
\]
then one-sided punctured arcs must enter either a good \(v_5\)-patch or the
parallel \(u_5\)-patch. On the \(v_5\)-patch side, the centered-to-patch bridge
then controls the explicit mixed low-order bad list
\[
(r,\operatorname{ord}_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}.
\]

\item
\textbf{Four-point nonmixed branch via deeper RH-specific identities.}
Generic local geometry already supports nonmixed odd-order exact branch sheets,
so the next theorem there is not a blanket sterility statement but a deeper
RH-specific parity / divisibility theorem forcing extra vanishing of
\[
\mathcal R=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2},
\]
equivalently of the nonmixed obstruction coefficients
\[
z_2,\ z_4,\ z_6.
\]

\item
\textbf{Route B backup degeneration tower.}
If the \(v_5\)-patch fails, the valuation theorem for
\[
\Delta_7=u_{7,K_1}v_5-u_5v_{7,K_1}
\]
forces matching late vanishing in the septic transport channel, and total
centered quintic collapse forces a source-level degeneration. Thus the failure
of the \(v_5\)-route is already confined to a narrow coupled degeneration
scheme rather than a free local cancellation.

\item
\textbf{Below-lifted RH-specific identities.}
Since the realization lemma shows that no definitive local closure can come
from the lifted variables alone, any final \(4\)-point closure theorem must
ultimately come from deeper source-level or matrix-level RH structure, for
example a witness-transport lemma for \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) or an RH-specific
divisibility / parity identity for
\[
\mathcal Z=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda}.
\]
\end{enumerate}
\end{remark}
```

This replacement aligns the “main route” with the quintic-patch dichotomy and demotes raw \(V_1\)-chasing to backup status, which matches where the chat ended up. turn90file18turn91file15

## 1) Add the missing automatic \(u_5\)-patch fallback corollary

This is a useful consequence that came out of the chat and is still not in the draft. It belongs **immediately after**
```latex
\begin{proposition}[Linear independence of $1,u_5/c,v_5/c$]
\label{prop:linear-independence-one-u5-over-c-v5-over-c}
...
\end{proposition}
```

Insert:

```latex
\begin{corollary}[Automatic \(u_5\)-patch on a good \(M\neq 0\) interval]
\label{cor:automatic-u5-patch-on-good-M-interval}
Let \(J\) be a connected open interval on which
\[
c\neq 0,
\qquad
M\neq 0.
\]
Then \(u_5\not\equiv 0\) on \(J\). Consequently, every connected component of
\[
J\setminus u_5^{-1}(0)
\]
is a valid local \(u_5\)-patch in the sense of
Remark~\ref{rem:parallel-u5-patch-version}.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
If \(u_5\equiv 0\) on \(J\), then the three functions
\[
1,\qquad \frac{u_5}{c},\qquad \frac{v_5}{c}
\]
would be linearly dependent, contradicting
Proposition~\ref{prop:linear-independence-one-u5-over-c-v5-over-c}. Thus
\(u_5\not\equiv 0\) on \(J\), so its zeros are isolated and each connected
component of \(J\setminus u_5^{-1}(0)\) lies in \(\{c\neq 0,\ u_5\neq 0\}\).
The parallel \(u_5\)-patch geometry then follows from
Remark~\ref{rem:parallel-u5-patch-version}.
\end{proof}
```

Why: this makes explicit a structural finding that is currently only implicit in the combination of the linear-independence proposition and the parallel \(u_5\)-patch remark. It strengthens the fallback geometry story in a useful, theorem-level way. turn98file4

## 2) Add the “full package collapse” corollary

The draft has the total centered quintic-collapse lemma, but it still helps to record the immediate septic consequence. Put this **immediately after**
```latex
\begin{lemma}[Total centered quintic collapse forces source-level degeneration]
\label{lem:total-centered-quintic-collapse}
...
\end{lemma}
```

Insert:

```latex
\begin{corollary}[Total centered quintic collapse forces total canonical transport collapse]
\label{cor:total-centered-quintic-collapse-forces-total-transport-collapse}
If
\[
u_5\equiv 0,
\qquad
v_5\equiv 0
\]
on the centered branch, then
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}\equiv 0,
\qquad
\Delta_7\equiv 0.
\]
In particular, total centered quintic collapse forces collapse of the canonical
quintic/septic transport package on that branch.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The identity
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5 I+v_5 S
\]
gives \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\equiv 0\) immediately. Likewise
\[
\Delta_7=u_{7,K_1}v_5-u_5v_{7,K_1}
\]
vanishes identically when \(u_5\equiv v_5\equiv 0\).
\end{proof}
```

Why: this “full package collapse” point was a real structural finding from the chat and is worth having explicitly in the paper. Right now it is still only implicit. turn90file18

## 3) Add the determinant-level parity remark for the centered good-patch bridge

This was a nice structural goodie from the chat and is still missing. Put it **immediately after**
```latex
\begin{remark}[Below-lifted Wronskian-ratio reformulation]
\label{rem:below-lifted-wronskian-ratio-reformulation}
...
\end{remark}
```

Insert:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Determinant-level parity on a centered good patch]
\label{rem:determinant-level-parity-centered-good-patch}
Assume the centered scalar package from
Remark~\ref{rem:centered-symmetric-placement-taylor-package} and suppose that
\(x=v_5/c\) is being used as the induced odd collision-side coordinate.
Then
\[
u_5,\ \lambda:=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}\ \text{are odd in }s,
\qquad
c\ \text{is even in }s,
\qquad
v_5\ \text{is odd in }s.
\]
Hence the rows of the defining determinants for \(J_{u_5}\) and \(J_\lambda\)
have parities
\[
(e,o,o),\qquad (o,e,e),\qquad (e,o,o),
\]
so each determinant monomial is odd. Therefore
\[
J_{u_5}(s)\ \text{and}\ J_\lambda(s)\ \text{are odd in }s.
\]
Consequently,
\[
\mathcal Z=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda}
\]
is even and
\[
\mathcal R=\mathcal Z'
\]
is odd, in agreement with the parity package obtained from the direct
\(Y''/S''\)-analysis.
\end{remark}
```

Why: this is a nice below-lifted structural identity that reinforces the mixed-side parity mechanism and ties the determinant route to the \(Y''/S''\) route. It is not in the draft now. turn98file7

## 6) Optional micro-polish in the centered witness lemma proof

This one is optional, but I think it reads a little more safely.

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Centered tagged quintic witness survives specialization]
\label{lem:centered-tagged-quintic-witness-survives-specialization}
```
