inside the proof, replace

```latex
Here $U_{12}$ supplies the tagged $\eta_2$-contribution to the off-diagonal
channel $v_0$, while $V_{22}$ supplies the tagged $q^{(5)}$-contribution
to the diagonal-difference channel $\gamma-\alpha=2\delta\alpha_1$. Thus the tagged coefficient of
$v_0\,\delta\alpha_1$ is nonzero. Therefore the tagged coefficient of $U_1$
is nonzero as well.
```

with

```latex
Here $U_{12}$ gives the tagged $\eta_2$-contribution to the off-diagonal
channel $v_0$, while $V_{22}$ gives the tagged $q^{(5)}$-contribution to the
diagonal-difference channel $\gamma-\alpha=2\delta\alpha_1$. Hence the tagged
coefficient of the product $v_0\,\delta\alpha_1$ is nonzero. Therefore the
tagged coefficient of $U_1$ is nonzero as well.
```

That keeps the argument the same, but makes the final step sound slightly less brittle.

## Assistant (2026-04-20 12:49:38)

I’m checking the current draft’s actual mixed \(4\)-point setup so I can phrase the two attack lanes in the paper’s current notation, not the older intermediate one.

_Thought for 1m 42s_

Yes — but the pincer is a little different now.

Earlier, both sides were trying to **prove** the mixed patch theorem. In the current draft, the centered quintic nontriviality / patch-dichotomy side is much further along, so the two sides of the pincer should now be:

## Left pincer: the **geometric / constructive** side

Start from the centered fixed-sector quintic package
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)=u_5(s)I+v_5(s)S.
\]
The right theorem-level target is that this does not vanish identically on the centered branch. Once you have that, the branch cannot have
\[
u_5\equiv 0,\qquad v_5\equiv 0,
\]
so on one-sided punctured arcs **some quintic patch opens**: either a good \(v_5\)-patch or the parallel \(u_5\)-patch. That is the patch-dichotomy route. turn104file7

Then the constructive side forks:

- If the \(v_5\)-patch opens, use
  \[
  x=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad
  Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad
  \lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},\qquad
  S=\frac{\lambda}{c},
  \]
  and try to complete the finite-jet centered-to-patch parity transfer. If that works, you get
  \[
  Y,S\ \text{odd},\qquad
  \mathcal Z=\frac{Y''}{S''}\ \text{even},\qquad
  \mathcal R=\mathcal Z'\ \text{odd},\qquad
  K_v=(x')^3S''\ \text{odd},
  \]
  which kills the explicit mixed bad list
  \[
  (r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}.
  \]
  turn103file4turn103file10turn104file12

- If instead only the \(u_5\)-patch opens, use the parallel local geometry
  \[
  Q_u(h)=\left(\frac{u_5}{c},\frac{v_5}{c},-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5}\right),
  \]
  and rebuild the local \(4\)-point analysis there rather than insisting on \(v_5\). The draft already has this patch available, so this is not ad hoc. turn104file7

So the left pincer is:

\[
\boxed{
A_5^{\mathfrak f}\not\equiv 0
\Longrightarrow
\text{some quintic patch opens}
\Longrightarrow
\text{do the local mixed analysis on that patch.}
}
\]

## Right pincer: the **obstructive / degeneration** side

Assume the nice \(v_5\)-route fails, or \(v_5\) starts late. Then do **not** chase a single coefficient like \(V_1\) anymore. Use Route B in its valuation form.

Write
\[
\Delta_7=u_{7,K_1}v_5-u_5v_{7,K_1}.
\]
If
\[
\ord_s u_5=2m+1,\qquad \ord_s v_5=2r+1,\qquad r\ge m,
\]
and
\[
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}
\]
stays analytic odd, then late vanishing of \(v_5\) forces matching late vanishing of the septic transport channel \(v_{7,K_1}\). In the earlier special case \(m=0\), this was the statement that if \(v_5\) starts late and \(U_1\neq 0\), then \(v_{7,K_1}\) must start at least as late; the valuation theorem is the cleaner general version. turn104file7turn86file0

And if the quintic pair totally collapses,
\[
u_5\equiv 0,\qquad v_5\equiv 0,
\]
then the centered germ system forces
\[
\begin{pmatrix}
\beta(s) & v(s)\\
\bar\alpha(s) & \bar u(s)
\end{pmatrix}
\binom{\delta u(s)}{\delta\alpha(s)}=0,
\]
so either
\[
\Delta_5(s):=\beta(s)\bar u(s)-v(s)\bar\alpha(s)\equiv 0
\]
or
\[
\delta u(s)\equiv \delta\alpha(s)\equiv 0.
\]
So failure of the patch theorem is not mild; it is a full centered degeneration. turn104file9

And once you reach any interval with
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad M\neq 0,
\]
the draft already gives linear independence of
\[
1,\qquad \frac{u_5}{c},\qquad \frac{v_5}{c},
\]
so in particular
\[
u_5\not\equiv 0
\]
there, which means the \(u_5\)-patch is automatically available as fallback. turn104file14

So the right pincer is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{if the }v_5\text{-patch route degenerates, force a quintic--septic valuation tower or total collapse,}
}
\]
and then show that this either contradicts analyticity/transport or pushes you into the \(u_5\)-patch anyway.

## How the two sides meet

They meet exactly where you want them to:

- The **left pincer** says: some quintic patch opens, so analyze the mixed branch on that patch.
- The **right pincer** says: if the preferred \(v_5\)-patch does **not** open cleanly, that failure is so rigid that it either collapses into the \(u_5\)-patch or into a tiny degeneration corner you can attack separately.

So the two-sided closure strategy is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{either the constructive patch opens and you kill the mixed bad list directly,}
}
\]
or
\[
\boxed{
\text{the patch fails in a highly constrained way, and the algebraic squeeze kills the failure mode.}
}
\]

## What I would assign to the two chats

If you want to run the same pincer again, I would split the work like this:

The **left/constructive chat** should focus on:

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}\not\equiv 0
\Longrightarrow
\text{patch dichotomy}
\Longrightarrow
\text{finite-jet parity transfer on the }v_5\text{-patch},
\]
and, if needed, start building the parallel local \(u_5\)-patch analysis.

The **right/obstructive chat** should focus on:

- the valuation tower for late vanishing of \(v_5\),
- the total-collapse alternatives
  \[
  \Delta_5\equiv 0 \quad\text{or}\quad \delta u\equiv\delta\alpha\equiv 0,
  \]
- and showing that failure of the \(v_5\)-route either contradicts the transport structure or automatically hands control to the \(u_5\)-patch.

So the answer is: **yes, a pincer still makes sense**, and the two sides are now much cleaner than before:

\[
\boxed{\text{Left: open and exploit a quintic patch.}}
\]
\[
\boxed{\text{Right: if the }v_5\text{-route degenerates, force collapse or fallback via Route B.}}
\]

That is the pincer I would use on the current draft.

}

Because once you have

\]
the coefficient algebra is already done: \(\mathcal Z\) has no \(x^1\) or \(x^3\) term, and \(K_v=(x')^3S''\) has odd vanishing order, so the whole mixed bad list dies. That part is already reduced to a finite low-order reparametrization check, not an all-orders mystery. turn108file10turn108file12

1. work in the centered symmetric-placement parameter \(s\), where
   \[

This is the constructive “fallback geometry” branch.

   \]

   \[

   \]
   with the same defect-free affine-dependence conclusions as on the \(v_5\)-patch. turn109file8

So the constructive side should no longer be framed as “first prove the \(v_5\)-patch opens, then work there.”  
The cleaner attack is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Use the }u_5\text{-patch as the primary local patch whenever the centered witness gives }U_1\neq 0.
}
\]

That is a real simplification.

## Why this is promising

On the centered branch, the draft already uses the parity package
\[
u_5(s),\,v_5(s),\,u_{7,K_1}(s),\,v_{7,K_1}(s)\ \text{odd in }s,
\qquad
\Delta_7(s)\ \text{even in }s,
\]
with explicit coefficients \(U_i,V_i,\widehat U_i,\widehat V_i,D_2,D_4,D_6\). turn110file18

If the centered tagged witness really gives
\[
U_1\neq 0,
\]
then
\[
x_u:=\frac{u_5}{c}
\]
is an odd local coordinate at the centered basepoint, because \(c(s)\) is even with nonzero constant term and \(u_5(s)=U_1s+O(s^3)\). Then on that same branch,
\[
Y_u:=\frac{v_5}{c}
\]
is odd, and
\[
S_u:=-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5}
\]
is also odd, since \(\Delta_7\) is even and \(c\,u_5\) is odd. So in the \(u_5\)-patch coordinate \(x_u\) one gets the exact same parity package the old \(v_5\)-route wanted:
\[
Y_u(x_u)\ \text{odd},\qquad
S_u(x_u)\ \text{odd}.
\]
Hence
\[
Y_u''(x_u),\ S_u''(x_u)\ \text{odd},
\qquad
\mathcal Z_u:=\frac{Y_u''}{S_u''}\ \text{even},
\qquad
\mathcal R_u:=\mathcal Z_u'\ \text{odd},
\]
and the corresponding curvature scalar
\[
K_u=(x_u')^3S_u''
\]
has odd vanishing order. turn110file11turn110file17

That is exactly the same finite-jet mechanism that killed the explicit mixed bad list on the \(v_5\)-side once parity transferred.

## The constructive theorem I would attack now

The right theorem is not “prove the \(v_5\)-patch opens.”

It is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The local mixed obstruction list is patch-invariant.}
}
\]

More concretely:

> If the local \(4\)-point mixed/nonmixed classification is derived only from the defect-free affine-dependence geometry of \(Q_v\), then the same classification holds verbatim for \(Q_u\), with the corresponding invariants \((K_u,T_u,\mathcal Z_u,\mathcal R_u)\).

Why this is plausible:
the draft explicitly says the same defect-free affine-dependence conclusions hold with \(Q_v\) replaced by \(Q_u\). So the whole local model analysis should be reproducible on the \(u_5\)-patch, not just the determinant identities.

1. centered witness gives \(U_1\neq 0\);
2. therefore the \(u_5\)-patch opens canonically at the centered basepoint;
3. in \(x_u=u_5/c\), the same odd/even parity package holds;
4. by patch-invariant local classification, the same explicit mixed bad list
   \[
   (r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}
   \]
   is the one to exclude;
5. parity on the \(u_5\)-patch excludes it immediately.

\Longrightarrow

}

That is cleaner than the old \(v_5/c\) bridge.

2. **Does the local mixed obstruction classification transfer verbatim from \(Q_v\) to \(Q_u\)?**

}

Because if that works, then the centered witness \(U_1\neq 0\) becomes immediately useful: you get a canonical local patch at the basepoint, and the parity transfer there is formal.

So my constructive attack is:

- stop insisting that the \(v_5\)-patch is the first thing to open;
- use the new centered witness to try to open the \(u_5\)-patch canonically;
- then show the same mixed obstruction list and parity-kill mechanism hold on \(Q_u\).

so the centered quintic pair does not totally collapse. And the draft already has a fully parallel \(u_5\)-patch geometry

## The constructive theorem to attack

Assume the centered witness lemma really gives
\[
U_1\neq 0.
\]
Then on the centered branch,
\[
u_5(s)=U_1s+U_3s^3+\cdots,
\qquad

so

is an odd local coordinate at the centered basepoint.

\[

\qquad

\]

\qquad
\Delta_7(s)\ \text{even in }s,

it follows immediately that
\[
x_u(s),\ Y_u(s),\ S_u(s)

are all odd in \(s\). Hence, after passing to the odd inverse \(s=s(x_u)\),

\qquad

\]

and the corresponding curvature scalar

has odd vanishing order. turn112file2turn112file1

\]

## So what is the exact remaining constructive gap?

It is no longer “prove the patch dichotomy.”  
And it is no longer “prove \(V_1\neq 0\).”

It is this:

Here is the strongest **Left Pincer** attack I can honestly make now:

The draft already gives a fully parallel \(u_5\)-patch:
\[

\]
and explicitly says the same defect-free affine-dependence conclusions hold with \(Q_v\) replaced by \(Q_u\). So the \(u_5\)-patch is not just a fallback notation; it is a genuine local geometric setting already built into the paper. turn114file1

That means the constructive side should no longer insist on opening the \(v_5\)-patch first. The cleaner route is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{if }U_1\neq 0,\text{ use }x_u:=u_5/c\text{ as the canonical local coordinate and run the mixed analysis on }Q_u.
}
\]

## Why this is better

On the centered branch, the paper’s centered Taylor package gives
\[
u_5,v_5,u_{7,K_1},v_{7,K_1}\ \text{odd in }s,\qquad \Delta_7\ \text{even in }s,
\]
with explicit coefficients \(U_i,V_i,\widehat U_i,\widehat V_i,D_2,D_4,D_6\). turn114file8

If the centered witness work really gives
\[
U_1\neq 0,
\]
then
\[
u_5(s)=U_1s+U_3s^3+\cdots,\qquad c(s)=c_0+c_2s^2+\cdots,\qquad c_0\neq 0,
\]
so
\[
x_u(s):=\frac{u_5(s)}{c(s)}
\]
is an odd local coordinate at the centered basepoint. Then the two other \(u_5\)-patch quantities
\[
Y_u:=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
S_u:=-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5}
\]
are also odd in \(s\): \(v_5\) is odd, \(c\) is even, \(\Delta_7\) is even, and \(c\,u_5\) is odd. Hence after passing to the odd inverse \(s=s(x_u)\),
\[
Y_u(x_u)\ \text{odd},\qquad S_u(x_u)\ \text{odd}.
\]
Therefore
\[
Y_u''(x_u),\ S_u''(x_u)\ \text{odd},\qquad
\mathcal Z_u:=\frac{Y_u''}{S_u''}\ \text{even},\qquad
\mathcal R_u:=\mathcal Z_u'\ \text{odd},
\]
and the corresponding curvature scalar
\[
K_u=(x_u')^3S_u''
\]
has odd vanishing order. turn114file10turn114file11

So on the \(u_5\)-patch, the parity package is actually cleaner than on the \(v_5\)-patch, because it uses the centered witness-driven \(U_1\neq 0\) rather than the harder \(V_1\neq 0\) route.

## The real constructive gap is now a patch-invariance lemma

The mixed local obstruction list on the \(v_5\)-patch was reduced to the finite possibilities
\[

\]
equivalently the low-order monomial models \((m,n)=(3,4),(3,6),(4,6)\). And that reduction came from the generic lifted-curve analysis of a triple
\[
Q=(Y,x,S),
\]
not from anything deeply specific to the symbol \(v_5\). turn113file9turn113file13

Since the draft already says the same defect-free affine-dependence conclusions hold for \(Q_u\) as for \(Q_v\), the natural constructive theorem to prove is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Patch-invariance lemma: the local mixed/nonmixed obstruction classification for }Q_v
\text{ carries over verbatim to }Q_u.
}
\]

If that lemma is true, then the rest is immediate: on \(Q_u\), parity gives
\[
\ord_0 K_u \text{ odd},\qquad \ord_0\mathcal Z_u \text{ even},
\]
so the same explicit mixed bad list is excluded at once.

In other words, the left pincer now looks like:

\[
\boxed{
U_1\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\text{canonical local }u_5\text{-patch}
\Longrightarrow
\text{odd/odd parity package on }Q_u
\Longrightarrow

}
\]

This is cleaner than the old \(v_5\)-bridge route because it avoids the brittle coefficient bottleneck \(V_1\neq 0\). It also matches the current draft’s structure better: the draft already treats the \(u_5\)-patch as a real parallel geometry, and once any connected interval with
\[

\]
is reached, the paper already proves linear independence of
\[

\]
so in particular \(u_5\not\equiv 0\) there; that means the \(u_5\)-patch is a real fallback local setting, not a speculative one. turn114file2

So my actual Left-Pincer conclusion is:

\[

\[

\]

\[

is impossible immediately: the first two violate evenness of \(\ord_0\mathcal Z\), and the third violates oddness of \(r=\ord_0K_v\). turn123file14turn123file16

one gets

So on the clean branch, \(M\) is already nonzero at the centered base. I think the remaining mixed local corner can be attacked harder than we were saying.

The right-pincer update already contains the key observation: on the centered branch, once the tagged witness gives
\[
U_1\neq 0,
\]
the \(u_5\)-patch is locally automatic because
\[

\]
is an odd local coordinate near the centered base. If the preferred \(v_5\)-route degenerates so that
\[

\]
then on that same \(u_5\)-patch
\[
x(y):=\frac{v_5}{c}=O(y^{2r+1}),
\]
so \(x(y)\) is an odd germ vanishing at least cubically. More importantly, even **without** assuming \(\lambda=\Delta_7/v_5\) stays analytic odd, one still has
\[
\tau_u:=-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5}
\]
odd, simply because \(\Delta_7\) is even while \(c\) is even and \(u_5\) is odd. Since \(\ord_s\Delta_7\ge 2\) and \(\ord_s u_5=1\), one gets \(\ord_s\tau_u\ge 1\). So on the \(u_5\)-patch the late-\(v_5\) corner always has the form
\[
Q_u(y)=\bigl(y,\ x(y),\ \tau_u(y)\bigr),
\qquad
x(y)\ \text{odd with }\ord_0x\ge 3,\qquad
\tau_u(y)\ \text{odd with }\ord_0\tau_u\ge 1.
\]
Subtract the linear part of \(\tau_u\):
\[
\widetilde\tau_u(y):=\tau_u(y)-\tau_u'(0)\,y.
\]
Then \(\widetilde\tau_u\) is odd and either vanishes identically or has odd order at least \(3\). After the fixed ambient coordinate permutation
\[
(y,x,\widetilde\tau_u)\longmapsto (x,y,\widetilde\tau_u),
\]
the germ becomes exactly the same odd/odd local model already used in the centered diagonal-base exclusion argument,
\[
\widetilde Q_u(y)\sim \bigl(y^n,\ y,\ y^m\bigr),
\qquad m,n\ \text{odd},\quad m,n\ge 3,
\]
or a degenerate case where one higher-order channel vanishes identically, which is even less dangerous. turn125file17turn125file18

And the existing centered diagonal-base local theorem already says that in that odd/odd model there is a punctured neighborhood with
\[
K_v\neq 0,\qquad T_v\neq 0,
\]
so no mixed or nonmixed \(4\)-point obstruction point is born there. turn125file9

So the key attack result is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the residual corner }V_1=0\text{ does not actually need }\lambda=\Delta_7/v_5\text{ analytic odd to look harmless locally.}
}
\]

The \(u_5\)-patch already gives an odd local coordinate, and after subtracting the linear part of \(\tau_u\) the late-\(v_5\) corner falls into the same odd/odd local sterility model anyway. The analytic-odd \(\lambda\) assumption was a stronger route to force \(\ord\tau_u\ge 2r+1\), but it is not obviously necessary for the basic local sterility transplant. turn125file17

So my honest updated map is:

- **clean branch \(V_1\neq 0\):** left pincer kills it on the \(v_5\)-patch by the centered-to-\(x=v_5/c\) parity transfer. turn123file16
- **late-\(v_5\) branch \(V_1=0\):** right pincer plausibly kills it on the automatically-open \(u_5\)-patch even without requiring \(\lambda\) analytic odd, because after affine normalization it is the same odd/odd sterile model. turn125file17turn125file0

That leaves, at least near the centered base, no obvious mixed local corner alive except the theorem-level task of writing the \(u_5\)-patch transplant carefully enough that the existing odd/odd sterility proof can be cited verbatim.

\[

I think the left pincer can now push the mixed local picture one step further.

is excluded because \(\mathcal Z\) is even and \(K_v\) has odd vanishing order. So the left pincer no longer needs to do anything on the clean \(v_5\)-patch branch. turn123file14turn123file16

What remains is the late-\(v_5\) branch, and here I think the right-pincer update can be strengthened.

Since the centered witness gives
\[
U_1\neq 0,
\]
the \(u_5\)-patch is automatically open near the centered base:
\[
y:=\frac{u_5}{c}
\]
is an odd local coordinate. On the late-\(v_5\) branch
\[
\ord_s v_5=2r+1\ge 3,
\]
so on the \(u_5\)-patch
\[
x(y):=\frac{v_5}{c}=O(y^{2r+1}),
\]
an odd germ vanishing at least cubically. Also
\[
\tau_u(y):=-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5}
\]
is always odd, because \(\Delta_7\) is even while \(c\) is even and \(u_5\) is odd. No analyticity assumption on \(\lambda=\Delta_7/v_5\) is needed for that basic parity. Thus the local \(u_5\)-patch curve has the form
\[
Q_u(y)=\bigl(y,\ x(y),\ \tau_u(y)\bigr),
\qquad
x(y)\ \text{odd with }\ord_0x\ge 3,\qquad
\tau_u(y)\ \text{odd with }\ord_0\tau_u\ge 1.
\]
turn126file5

Now subtract the linear part of \(\tau_u\):
\[
\widetilde\tau_u(y):=\tau_u(y)-\tau_u'(0)\,y.
\]
Then \(\widetilde\tau_u\) is odd and either vanishes identically or has odd order at least \(3\). This gives a clean dichotomy.

If
\[
\widetilde\tau_u\not\equiv 0,
\]
then after the fixed ambient coordinate permutation
\[
(y,x,\widetilde\tau_u)\mapsto (x,y,\widetilde\tau_u)
\]
and, if needed, subtraction of a suitable odd multiple of \(\widetilde\tau_u\) from \(x\) to separate the leading odd orders, the germ reduces to the same odd/odd local normal form
\[
(y^n,\ y,\ y^m),
\qquad
m,n\ \text{odd},\quad m,n\ge 3,
\]
already used in the centered diagonal-base sterility theorem. Since the proof there is purely local and affine-geometric, it applies verbatim after this normalization. So this whole subcase is locally sterile on punctured \(u_5\)-patch arcs. turn126file5

So the only genuinely remaining mixed local corner is the complementary case
\[
\widetilde\tau_u\equiv 0,
\]
that is, \(\tau_u\) is exactly linear in the \(u_5\)-patch coordinate:
\[
\tau_u(y)=a\,y
\]
for some constant \(a\). Rewriting this in the original scalars gives the sharp residual algebraic relation
\[
-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5}=a\,\frac{u_5}{c}
\qquad\Longleftrightarrow\qquad
\Delta_7=-a\,u_5^2.
\]
So the late-\(v_5\) corner is now reduced to one explicit possibility:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Residual mixed local corner: }\Delta_7 \text{ is locally proportional to }u_5^2\text{ on the }u_5\text{-patch.}
}
\]

That is much sharper than where we were before. It means:

- clean branch \(V_1\neq 0\): killed by the left pincer on the \(v_5\)-patch; turn123file16
- late-\(v_5\) branch with \(\widetilde\tau_u\not\equiv 0\): killed by the right-pincer odd/odd sterility transplant on the \(u_5\)-patch; turn126file5
- only remaining mixed local corner near the centered base:
  \[
  \Delta_7=-a\,u_5^2.
  \]

So the next exact theorem to attack is no longer “patch opening” or “late \(v_5\) valuation tower.” It is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{rule out or exploit the special relation }\Delta_7\propto u_5^2\text{ on the }u_5\text{-patch.}
}
\]

That is now the narrowest mixed-side corner I can see.

\Delta_7=-a\,u_5^2
\ \text{locally on the }u_5\text{-patch.}
}
\]

left alive on that side. 

From the **left-pincer** point of view, this means my task is now fully narrowed:

\[
\boxed{
\text{I only need to handle the branch }\ord_s v_5=1.
}
\]

On that branch,
\[
v_5(s)=V_1s+V_3s^3+\cdots,\qquad V_1\neq 0,
\]
so
\[
x(s)=\frac{v_5}{c}=X_1s+X_3s^3+\cdots,\qquad X_1=\frac{V_1}{C_0}\neq 0,
\]
and therefore the good \(v_5\)-patch is already open locally. So there is no remaining patch-opening problem on my side at all. The only theorem left for me is the finite-jet bridge:
\[
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}
\]
are odd mod \(O(x^7)\) in
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\]
which kills
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}
\]
immediately. 

There is one extra observation I’d add to the right-pincer picture.

If the residual corner really is
\[
\Delta_7=-a\,u_5^2,
\]
then on the \(u_5\)-patch
\[
\tau_u:=-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5}=a\,\frac{u_5}{c}=a\,y.
\]
So after subtracting the linear part, the third channel vanishes identically:
\[
\widetilde\tau_u\equiv 0.
\]
That means the residual corner is not a generic three-channel lifted germ anymore. After normalization it collapses to
\[
Q_u(y)\sim (y,\ x(y),\ 0),
\qquad x(y)=O(y^{2r+1}),\ r\ge 1.
\]
So the remaining bad corner is actually a **rank-two / planar** local model, not a full 3D one. That is an even sharper target than “late \(v_5\) on \(Q_u\).” 

So the clean next attacks are now:

- **Left pincer:** prove the finite-jet clean-\(v_5\)-patch bridge on the \(\ord_s v_5=1\) branch.
- **Right pincer:** attack the planar residual corner
  \[
  \Delta_7=-a\,u_5^2
  \]
  on \(Q_u\), since after subtracting the linear part of \(\tau_u\) the third channel disappears entirely. 

That is the best combined map I see now.

## User (2026-04-20 14:28:27)

ok formulate that lemma

## Assistant (2026-04-20 14:28:56)

_Thought for 19s_

Yes. Here is the draft-ready version I would use.

I’d actually formulate it as a **pair**: a main local trichotomy lemma, then a short corollary saying the only genuinely new branch left for the mixed analysis is the clean \(V_1\neq 0\) branch.

## Main lemma

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Local trichotomy for the mixed branch near the centered base]
\label{lem:local-trichotomy-mixed-branch-centered-base}
Assume the centered branch is in the centered symmetric-placement regime, and
assume the centered tagged quintic witness gives
\[
U_1\neq 0.
\]
Then
\[
u_5(s)=U_1s+U_3s^3+\cdots
\]
has a simple odd zero at the centered base, so with
\[
c(s)=C_0+O(s^2),
\qquad
C_0\neq 0,
\]
the \(u_5\)-patch coordinate
\[
y:=\frac{u_5}{c}
\]
is an odd local coordinate near the centered base.

Let
\[
x(y):=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
\tau_u(y):=-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5},
\qquad
\widetilde\tau_u(y):=\tau_u(y)-\tau_u'(0)\,y.
\]
Then every sufficiently small nearby mixed \(4\)-point branch falls into exactly
one of the following three local regimes:

\begin{enumerate}
\item[(i)] \textbf{Clean \(v_5\)-branch:}
\[
\ord_s v_5=1.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
v_5(s)=V_1s+V_3s^3+\cdots,
\qquad
V_1\neq 0.
\]
Then
\[
x(s)=\frac{v_5(s)}{c(s)}=X_1s+X_3s^3+\cdots,
\qquad
X_1=\frac{V_1}{C_0}\neq 0,
\]
so \(x=v_5/c\) is an odd local coordinate and the branch lies locally in a
genuine good \(v_5\)-patch.

\item[(ii)] \textbf{Late \(v_5\)-branch with nontrivial \(u_5\)-patch lift:}
\[
\ord_s v_5=2r+1\ge 3,
\qquad
\widetilde\tau_u\not\equiv 0.
\]
Then \(x(y)\) and \(\widetilde\tau_u(y)\) are odd germs, and
\[
x(y)=O(y^{2r+1}),
\qquad
\ord_0 x\ge 3,
\qquad
\ord_0 \widetilde\tau_u\ge 3.
\]
After an ambient coordinate permutation
\[
(y,x,\widetilde\tau_u)\mapsto (x,y,\widetilde\tau_u)
\]
and, if needed, subtraction of a suitable odd multiple to separate equal
leading odd orders, the germ reduces to the odd/odd local normal form
\[
(y^n,\ y,\ y^m),
\qquad
n>m\ge 3,
\qquad
m,n\ \text{odd},
\]
or to a simpler degenerate case with one higher-order channel identically zero.

\item[(iii)] \textbf{Residual planar-lift corner:}
\[
\ord_s v_5=2r+1\ge 3,
\qquad
\widetilde\tau_u\equiv 0.
\]
Then \(\tau_u(y)=a\,y\) for some constant \(a\), equivalently
\[
-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5}=a\,\frac{u_5}{c}
\qquad\Longleftrightarrow\qquad
\Delta_7=-a\,u_5^2.
\]
In this case
\[
Q_u=(y,x,ay),
\]
so after the ambient shear
\[
(Y,X,Z)\mapsto (Y,X,Z-aY)
\]
the lifted \(u_5\)-patch curve becomes
\[
Q_u\sim (y,x,0),
\]
hence is affine-planar.
\end{enumerate}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Because \(U_1\neq 0\), the germ \(u_5(s)\) has order \(1\), hence
\[
y=\frac{u_5}{c}
\]
is an odd local coordinate.

Since \(v_5\) is odd on the centered branch, either \(\ord_s v_5=1\) or
\(\ord_s v_5=2r+1\ge 3\) is odd. This gives the dichotomy between (i) and
the late-\(v_5\) cases (ii)--(iii).

In case (i),
\[
x(s)=\frac{v_5(s)}{c(s)}=X_1s+X_3s^3+\cdots
\]
with \(X_1=V_1/C_0\neq 0\), so \(x\) is an odd local coordinate. Moreover,
\[
x'=\left(\frac{v_5}{c}\right)'=\frac{M}{c^2},
\]
hence
\[
M(0)=c(0)^2x'(0)=C_0V_1\neq 0,
\]
so the branch lies locally in a genuine good \(v_5\)-patch.

Now assume \(\ord_s v_5=2r+1\ge 3\). Because \(v_5\) is odd and \(c\) is even,
\[
x(y)=\frac{v_5}{c}
\]
is odd, with
\[
x(y)=O(y^{2r+1}),
\]
so \(\ord_0 x\ge 3\). Also \(\Delta_7\) is even while \(c\) is even and \(u_5\)
is odd, hence
\[
\tau_u(y)=-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5}
\]
is odd. Therefore \(\widetilde\tau_u(y)=\tau_u(y)-\tau_u'(0)y\) is odd and
either vanishes identically or has odd order at least \(3\).

If \(\widetilde\tau_u\not\equiv 0\), then after the stated ambient coordinate
permutation and, if needed, subtraction of a suitable odd multiple to separate
equal leading odd orders, the germ reduces to the displayed odd/odd local
normal form, yielding (ii).

If \(\widetilde\tau_u\equiv 0\), then \(\tau_u(y)=a\,y\) for some constant
\(a\), which is equivalent to
\[
\Delta_7=-a\,u_5^2.
\]
Then
\[
Q_u=(y,x,ay),
\]
and the stated ambient shear makes the third coordinate vanish identically,
yielding the planar-lift form (iii).
\end{proof}
```

## Corollary that says what this buys you

```latex
\begin{corollary}[Local reduction of the mixed branch near the centered base]
\label{cor:local-reduction-mixed-branch-centered-base}
Assume the odd/odd local sterility theorem applies to the normalized odd/odd
model in Lemma~\ref{lem:local-trichotomy-mixed-branch-centered-base}(ii). Then
every sufficiently small nearby mixed \(4\)-point obstruction branch near the
centered base is reduced to one of the following two possibilities:

\begin{enumerate}
\item[(a)] the clean branch \(\ord_s v_5=1\), on which the good \(v_5\)-patch is
already open locally and the remaining task is the finite-jet parity transfer
in
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c};
\]

\item[(b)] the planar-lift corner
\[
\Delta_7=-a\,u_5^2
\]
on the \(u_5\)-patch.
\end{enumerate}
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
By Lemma~\ref{lem:local-trichotomy-mixed-branch-centered-base}, every
sufficiently small nearby mixed branch falls into one of the three regimes
(i)--(iii). Regime (ii) reduces to the odd/odd local normal form already known
to be punctured-neighborhood sterile, so it cannot support a nearby mixed
obstruction branch. The only remaining possibilities are (i) and (iii).
\end{proof}
```

## If you want an even shorter “right-pincer lemma” instead

If you prefer something more surgical, this is the compact version:

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Right-pincer \(u_5\)-patch transplant]
\label{lem:right-pincer-u5-patch-transplant}
Assume \(U_1\neq 0\), so \(y=u_5/c\) is an odd local coordinate near the
centered base. If
\[
\ord_s v_5=2r+1\ge 3,
\]
then on the \(u_5\)-patch
\[
Q_u(y)=\left(y,\ x(y),\ \tau_u(y)\right),
\qquad
x(y)=\frac{v_5}{c}=O(y^{2r+1}),
\qquad
\tau_u(y)=-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5},
\]
with \(x\) and \(\tau_u\) odd. Let
\[
\widetilde\tau_u(y):=\tau_u(y)-\tau_u'(0)\,y.
\]
If \(\widetilde\tau_u\not\equiv 0\), then after an ambient coordinate swap and,
if needed, subtraction of a suitable odd multiple to separate equal leading odd
orders, the germ reduces to the same odd/odd local normal form already shown
punctured-neighborhood sterile. If \(\widetilde\tau_u\equiv 0\), then
\[
\Delta_7=-a\,u_5^2
\]
for some constant \(a\), and \(Q_u\) is affine-planar after an ambient shear.
\end{lemma}
```

That is the exact theorem-level statement the right pincer has been converging toward. It matches the split you and the other chat ended with. 

If you want, next I can turn this into an insertion targeted to the current draft, with “insert after X / before Y” placement.

## Assistant (2026-04-20 14:47:00)

I think there is one more real step: attack the planar residual corner directly and try to absorb it into the already-known quintic-circuit regime, instead of treating it as a new mixed/septic phenomenon.

_Thought for 26s_

Yes. I think there is one more real step, and it is the natural next attack.

The residual corner from the right pincer was

\[
\Delta_7=-a\,u_5^2
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
Q_u\sim (y,x,0),
\qquad
y=\frac{u_5}{c},\ x=\frac{v_5}{c}.
\]

That means the lifted \(u_5\)-patch curve is affine-planar. Once you say that out loud, the right question is no longer “can a new mixed septic \(4\)-point branch survive here?” The right question is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does an affine-planar }Q_u\text{ corner produce anything beyond the already-known quintic circuit regime?}
}
\]

I think the answer is very likely **no**, and that is the next attack.

## The sharper attack

In the planar corner,
\[
Q_u(h)=\bigl(y(h),x(h),0\bigr)
\]
after an ambient shear. So any affine \(4\)-point coplanarity condition for lifted points of \(Q_u\) is automatic. The only remaining nontrivial content is the affine dependence of the planar pair
\[
\Xi(h):=(y(h),x(h))=\left(\frac{u_5(h)}{c(h)},\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)}\right).
\]

That is exactly the order-\(\le 5\) quintic geometry, not a genuinely new order-\(\le 7\) lifted geometry.

So the residual corner should be attacked by the following lemma.

---

### Proposed next lemma: planar-lift absorption

\[
\boxed{
\text{If }Q_u\text{ is locally affine-planar, then any nearby defect-free }4\text{-point obstruction on }Q_u
\text{ reduces to a defect-free affine circuit of }\Xi=(u_5/c,\ v_5/c).
}
\]

Why this should be true:

A defect-free \(4\)-point obstruction in the lifted picture is meaningful only because the lift adds nontrivial affine content. But if the lift is planar, that extra affine content disappears. After shearing to
\[
Q_u\sim (y,x,0),
\]
the lifted \(4\)-point problem is just the planar affine dependence problem for the projected points \((y_i,x_i)\). That is precisely the quintic circuit regime the draft already isolates at order \(\le 5\). 

So the residual corner is not a new mixed/septic obstruction. It is an old quintic-circuit corner in disguise.

---

## What this would buy us

If that lemma is right, then the local mixed picture near the centered base becomes:

1. **Clean branch**
   \[
   \ord_s v_5=1.
   \]
   Then the good \(v_5\)-patch is already open and the left pincer kills the explicit mixed low-order list by the \(x=v_5/c\) parity transfer. 

2. **Late-\(v_5\) branch with \(\widetilde\tau_u\not\equiv 0\)**
   This is killed by the odd/odd sterility transplant on the automatic \(u_5\)-patch. 

3. **Late-\(v_5\) branch with \(\widetilde\tau_u\equiv 0\)**
   Equivalently
   \[
   \Delta_7=-a\,u_5^2,
   \]
   and then the lifted curve is planar, so the branch reduces to the already-known quintic circuit regime rather than a new mixed/septic branch. 

That would mean:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Near the centered base, there is no genuinely new mixed }4\text{-point local geometry left.}
}
\]

That is a real further attack.

## The one caveat

I would not claim this is fully proved yet. The missing theorem-level step is exactly the planar-lift absorption lemma above. It feels very plausible, but it still needs to be written carefully in the draft’s own defect-free language.

In particular, the statement has to be something like:

- after shearing to \(Q_u\sim(y,x,0)\),
- any minimal bad \(4\)-point lifted configuration projects to a minimal bad affine circuit of \(\Xi=(y,x)\),
- hence the corner is absorbed by the paper’s existing order-\(\le 5\) finite-core / circuit analysis.

That is what needs formalizing.

## So, yes, we can attack further

The next exact theorem to push is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Planar-lift absorption lemma: }Q_u\sim(y,x,0)\text{ implies the residual corner is not a new mixed/septic branch.}
}
\]

If that falls, then the combined pincer has essentially cornered the mixed local branch near the centered base.

If you want, I’ll write that lemma and proof sketch in draft-ready LaTeX.

_Thought for 1m 39s_

Yes. One more real step is possible, but it does **not** give a full contradiction. It gives a cleaner reduction.

The strongest further attack I can honestly make is this:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The residual corner }\Delta_7=-a\,u_5^2\text{ is not a genuinely new mixed/septic }4\text{-point geometry.}
}
\]

Here is the clean argument.

On the \(u_5\)-patch,
\[
Q_u(h)=\left(\frac{u_5(h)}{c(h)},\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},-\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)u_5(h)}\right).
\]
If the residual relation
\[
\Delta_7=-a\,u_5^2
\]
holds locally, then with
\[
y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\]
the third coordinate becomes
\[
\tau_u=-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5}=a\,\frac{u_5}{c}=a\,y.
\]
So
\[
Q_u=(y,x,ay).
\]
After the ambient shear
\[
(Y,X,Z)\mapsto (Y,X,Z-aY),
\]
this becomes
\[
Q_u\sim (y,x,0).
\]
So the residual corner is an **affine-planar lift**. turn134file0

Once you are in that form, coplanarity of four lifted points is automatic. The only remaining nontrivial content is affine dependence of the planar pair
\[
\Xi(h):=\left(\frac{u_5(h)}{c(h)},\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)}\right).
\]
But the draft already has exactly that order-\(\le 5\) reduction: defect-free bad cores imply affine dependence of the points \(\Xi(h_j)\), and minimal bad quintic circuits have size at most four. So the planar-lift corner is not a new order-\(\le 7\) mixed obstruction; it collapses back into the already-known **quintic circuit regime**. turn134file4

So the honest strengthened statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Near the centered base, every late-}v_5\text{ branch is either}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{(a) locally sterile on }Q_u,\ \text{or}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{(b) planar-lift and therefore absorbed into the quintic-circuit regime.}
}
\]

This is stronger than saying the late branch is merely “rigid.” It says the only residual late-\(v_5\) corner is no longer a genuinely new mixed/septic branch at all. turn130file0

The one place I would still be careful is this:

this does **not** by itself kill the planar corner outright, because affine \(4\)-point circuits in the plane are generic. What it does do is remove that corner from the “new mixed \(4\)-point/septic” agenda and hand it off to the paper’s existing order-\(\le 5\) finite-core/quintic-circuit machinery. turn134file3

So the best further attack summary is now:

- clean branch \(V_1\neq 0\): left pincer owns it on the genuine good \(v_5\)-patch; 
- late branch with \(\widetilde\tau_u\not\equiv 0\): right pincer owns it via the odd/odd sterility transplant on \(Q_u\); turn133file4
- late branch with \(\widetilde\tau_u\equiv 0\): not a new mixed/septic branch, but a planar quintic-circuit corner. turn134file2

So, yes, we can attack further, and I think this is the farthest honest push:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The right pincer locally disposes of every late-}v_5\text{ branch as either sterile or already-quintic.}
}
\]

That leaves the only genuinely new mixed local work near the centered base on the **clean \(V_1\neq 0\) branch**, which is exactly the left-pincer finite-jet parity bridge.

## Left pincer: attack only the clean \(V_1\neq 0\) branch

This side should stop worrying about patch opening or late-\(v_5\) degeneration. On the clean branch,
\[
v_5(s)=V_1s+V_3s^3+\cdots,\qquad V_1\neq 0,
\]
so
\[
x(s)=\frac{v_5(s)}{c(s)}=X_1s+X_3s^3+X_5s^5+\cdots
\]
is already the good local coordinate. The only theorem left here is the finite-jet bridge:
\[
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}
\]
are odd mod \(O(x^7)\). Once that is proved, the whole explicit mixed bad list
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}
\]
dies immediately. turn149file18turn148file15

The best way to push this is **not** as a vague parity theorem. It is a finite computation. The notes already reduce it to the statement that, on the relevant centered branch, the scalar denominator \(c\) has no odd jets through order \(5\):
\[
c_1=c_3=c_5=0.
\]
If that holds, then \(Y=u_5/c\) is odd through \(O(s^7)\), and since \(\lambda=\Delta_7/v_5\) is already odd, the same is true for
\[
S=\frac{\lambda}{c},
\]
hence oddness transfers through the odd inverse \(s(x)\) and the mixed list is gone. So the clean left-pincer target is really:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Fixed-sector scalar descent target: prove }c_1=c_3=c_5=0\text{ on the relevant centered branch.}
}
\]

That is the sharpest way to phrase the left job now. turn149file15

If the other chat prefers a more structural route, the equivalent target is: prove the normalization stack is reflection-equivariant **through the finite jet order needed for**
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6),
\]
rather than in full generality. Same theorem, different packaging. 

## Right pincer: stop doing new local jet algebra; move to absorption and local reduction

The local late-\(v_5\) geometry is now basically classified. So the right pincer should no longer spend time squeezing more coefficients.

It should do two things.

First, make the current theorem package airtight:

- the \(Q_u\) affine-normalization transplant lemma for \(\widetilde\tau_u\not\equiv 0\);
- the planar-lift absorption lemma for \(\widetilde\tau_u\equiv 0\), i.e.
  \[
  \Delta_7=-a\,u_5^2 \Longrightarrow Q_u\sim(y,x,0).
  \]

Those are now the real right-pincer lemmas, and they are the ones that let you say every late-\(v_5\) branch is either locally sterile or already-quintic. turn149file19

Second, once those are in place, the right pincer should push the **local reduction corollary**:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Any sufficiently small nearby genuinely new mixed }4\text{-point obstruction near the centered base must lie on the branch }\ord_s v_5=1.
}
\]

That is the exact handoff point to the left pincer. The right side should try to make that corollary explicit in the draft, because once it is theorem-level, the whole mixed local problem has been reduced to the left-pincer clean branch. turn146file0

There is one extra useful thing the right pincer can still attack: in the planar corner \(Q_u\sim(y,x,0)\), show explicitly that this is absorbed by the defect-free quintic-circuit regime for
\[
\Xi=\left(\frac{u_5}{c},\frac{v_5}{c}\right)
\]
and does not define a genuinely new mixed septic branch. The new finite-core/quintic-circuit block makes this much less speculative than before. turn149file17

## How the two pincers should meet

The joint goal should now be:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Right pincer proves: every late-}v_5\text{ branch is sterile or already-quintic.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Left pincer proves: on the remaining clean branch }V_1\neq 0,\ Y,S\equiv\text{odd}\pmod{O(x^7)}.
}
\]

If both close, then **locally near the centered base** the mixed \(4\)-point branch is exhausted. Any remaining escape is then no longer a new local mixed septic mechanism; it has to be global/nonlocal. turn149file3

So, in practical terms:

The **left pincer** should now spend all its time on the finite-jet bridge, preferably via the scalar descent target \(c_1=c_3=c_5=0\). 

The **right pincer** should now spend all its time on theorem-level packaging and absorption: the \(Q_u\) transplant lemma, the planar-lift absorption lemma, and the local reduction corollary that only \(\ord_s v_5=1\) remains. turn149file19

That is how I would keep pushing.

## 1) Make the local-reduction corollary cite the lemmas directly, not the remark

```latex
\begin{proof}

\[
\operatorname{ord}_s v_5=1
\qquad\text{or}\qquad
\operatorname{ord}_s v_5\ge 3 \text{ odd}.
\]

locally sterile on the $u_5$-patch or planar-lift and hence already-quintic.

cannot lie on such a late-$v_5$ branch. Therefore any such genuinely new
mixed local branch must lie on the only remaining possibility,
\[
\operatorname{ord}_s v_5=1.
\qedhere
\]
\end{proof}
```

with

```latex
\begin{proof}
Because $v_5$ is odd in the centered variable, either
\[
\operatorname{ord}_s v_5=1
\qquad\text{or}\qquad
\operatorname{ord}_s v_5\ge 3 \text{ odd}.
\]
If $\operatorname{ord}_s v_5\ge 3$, then
Lemma~\ref{lem:late-v5-u5-patch-transplant} and
Lemma~\ref{lem:planar-lift-absorption-u5-patch}
show that the branch is either locally sterile on the $u_5$-patch or
planar-lift and hence already-quintic. So a sufficiently small nearby
genuinely new mixed $4$-point obstruction cannot lie on such a late-$v_5$
branch. Therefore any such genuinely new mixed local branch must lie on the
only remaining possibility,
\[
\operatorname{ord}_s v_5=1.
\qedhere
\]
\end{proof}
```

```latex
...
\end{remark}
```

is really theorem content, not commentary.

```latex
\begin{corollary}[Right-pincer trichotomy near the centered base]
\label{cor:right-pincer-trichotomy-centered-base}
Near the centered diagonal base, the mixed local picture is reduced to the
following three cases:
\[

\Longrightarrow
\text{clean }v_5\text{-patch branch;}

\Longleftrightarrow
\Delta_7=-a\,u_5^2
\Longrightarrow
\text{planar-lift corner, hence already-quintic.}

or already absorbed into the quintic-circuit regime. The only genuinely new
mixed local branch left to study there is the clean branch
\[
\operatorname{ord}_s v_5=1.
\]
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Combine Lemma~\ref{lem:late-v5-u5-patch-transplant} and
Lemma~\ref{lem:planar-lift-absorption-u5-patch}, together with the fact that
$v_5$ is odd in the centered variable.
\end{proof}
```

```latex

```
to
```latex
Corollary~\ref{cor:right-pincer-trichotomy-centered-base}
```

are odd through the jet order needed, so \(\mathcal Z=Y''/S''\) is even and \(K_v=(x')^3S''\) has odd vanishing order, which kills the full explicit mixed bad list
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}.

The best attack on that scalar statement is a **finite equivariant-slice argument**, not more Taylor grinding.

Write the centered reflection operator on the one-pair normalization data as
\[
\Sigma(M)(s):=J_0\,M(-s)\,J_0.
\]
The current notes already isolate the crucial precursor fact: through the first residual quintic level, the quotient-level odd ambiguity is forced into the \(J_0\)-anti-fixed sector. That means the surviving odd ambiguity is traceless / off-scalar in exactly the direction where it should not contaminate the scalar normalization \(c\). So the natural theorem to attack is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Through jet order }5,\ \text{the normalization stack is }\Sigma\text{-equivariant on the scalar channel.}
}
\]

Concretely, the proof should try to show three steps.

First, the raw same-point / whitening data on the centered symmetric branch are \(\Sigma\)-fixed to the required jet order. Since \(s\mapsto -s\) swaps the microscopic points, this is the natural symmetry level where even/odd half-sum / half-difference structure lives. turn156file16

Second, the residual quotient/gauge directions through the quintic stage lie in the \(J_0\)-anti-fixed sector, so they can affect the odd fixed-sector package \((u_5,v_5)\) but should not contribute to the scalar fixed-sector normalization \(c\) through the low jet order we care about. That is the finite-dimensional content of the earlier involution route, and it is exactly where the current file says the quotient-level involution is already closed at first residual quintic order. turn156file4turn156file9

Third, once those two facts are combined, the scalar channel must be even through order \(5\):
\[
c_1=c_3=c_5=0.
\]
Then the left-pincer bridge is done. The centered odd/even package survives into the clean good-patch coordinate \(x=v_5/c\), and the mixed low-order list dies in one stroke. turn157file5turn157file8

So my honest attack result is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The remaining left-pincer problem is no longer “prove mixed exclusion.” It is “prove scalar evenness of }c\text{ through jet }5.”}
\]

That is much smaller than the old “full centered-to-patch parity theorem.”

And the division of labor is now very sharp:

The **left pincer** should work only on the finite scalar descent theorem
\[
c_1=c_3=c_5=0

]

depending on which determinant is generically nonzero on the clean branch.

just as the note suggests. The point is that (\Psi^{\mathrm{mix}}_a) uses both the (Y)- and (S)-channels, so it evades the no-go lemma that blocks any (S)-only argument.

### Mixed source-minor ratio lemma

On the clean branch (V_1\neq 0), define the repeated-source mixed ratio (\Psi^{\mathrm{mix}}*a(h)) from the source minors (D*{u_5}(a,h)) and (D_\lambda(a,h)). Prove that:

* it is well defined on the repeated-source clean branch;
* its derivative is controlled by a single (4\times 4) determinant, exactly as in the nonmixed repeated-source story;
* under the centered reflection (s\mapsto -s), it has a definite parity/sign behavior compatible with the expected evenness of (c). 

If that can be done, then the clean-branch parity bridge is no longer a vague chart argument; it becomes a source-determinant symmetry theorem.

Use the nonmixed “first loss of quadratic-envelope monotonicity rigidifies into repeated-node tangency” as a model. The mixed analogue would be:

* assume the clean-branch finite-jet oddness of (Y,S) fails for the first time;
* package that failure into the first sign/monotonicity loss of the mixed source ratio (\Psi^{\mathrm{mix}}_a);
* prove that first loss rigidifies into a lower-core repeated-node tangency or planar/quintic-circuit configuration, which is already handled by the existing infrastructure. 

This is where the “first-loss rigidification” update is genuinely useful: it gives a template for what a mixed contradiction should look like, rather than leaving the clean branch as a pure algebraic parity problem.

]

[

dies immediately.

The strongest way to formulate it is:

[
\boxed{
\text{anti-fixed/traceless quintic ambiguity cannot leak into the scalar channel through jet }5.
}
]

Why this is the right target:

The gauge law keeps the cubic coefficient fixed and changes the quintic coefficient only by the standard cubic-line/gauge terms, so the first residual ambiguity lives in the order-(5) anti-fixed traceless sector. That sector is structurally the wrong channel to create a scalar contribution by itself. Through order (5), the quotient-level swap involution already forces the quintic ambiguity into the (J_0)-anti-fixed traceless space; what is still missing is descent of that symmetry through the scalar normalization/gauge-fixing step.

So the exact theorem package to attack is:

[
\boxed{
\text{Finite-jet scalar descent theorem.}
}
]

A clean proof skeleton is:

1. Define the centered reflection on the raw corrected germ:
   [
   \Sigma(F)(z)=J_0F(-z)J_0.
   ]
   The draft already has this involutive structure at the raw/quintic level.

2. Show the scalar normalization condition is (\Sigma)-invariant through jet (5), and that its solution is unique through jet (5). This is the one place the theorem can still fail. The notes already say the real issue is not raw symmetry, but whether gauge-fixing/normalization commutes with the centered reflection.

3. Use the cubic-line argument. If the normalized cubic term is
   [
   A_3(s)=c(s),D,
   ]
   with fixed diagonal-traceless (D) satisfying
   [
   J_0DJ_0=-D,
   ]
   and the normalized family is reflection-equivariant, then
   [
   A_3(-s)=-J_0A_3(s)J_0=c(s)D.
   ]
   But also by definition
   [
   A_3(-s)=c(-s)D.
   ]
   Hence
   [
   c(-s)=c(s),
   ]
   so (C_1=C_3=C_5=0). This is the clean conceptual reason (c) should be even; it is not a miracle coefficient cancellation.

[

}
]

And even more sharply:

[
\boxed{
\text{The only place the clean mixed branch can still fail is if the scalar normalization/gauge-fixing does not commute with the centered reflection through jet }5.
}
]

That is the exact line-by-line theorem I would attack next in the current draft.

  [

* through order (5), the quotient-level quintic ambiguity is forced into the (J_0)-anti-fixed traceless sector;
* the gauge law keeps the cubic coefficient fixed and only changes the quintic coefficient by the usual cubic-line/gauge terms.

> On the clean centered branch (V_1\neq 0), the scalar normalization rule selecting (c(s)) from the centered normalized cubic line is (\Sigma)-equivariant through jet (5), and its solution is unique through jet (5). Hence
> [

> ]
> i.e.
> [

> ]

This is the minimal theorem now.

If the normalized cubic coefficient on the centered branch has the form
[
A_3(s)=c(s),D
]
for a fixed diagonal-traceless direction (D), and

]

But by definition of the scalar extraction,
[

]
So
[
c(-s)=c(s).
]
This is the conceptual reason (c) should be even: not because of a miraculous coefficient cancellation, but because the scalar (c) is the coefficient of an anti-fixed cubic line that becomes fixed after the extra minus sign in the reflection law.

On the clean centered branch \(V_1\neq 0\), the scalar normalization rule selecting \(c(s)\) from the normalized cubic line is reflection-equivariant through jet \(5\), and its output is unique through jet \(5\). Hence
\[
c(-s)-c(s)=O(s^6).
\]

The conceptual mechanism is the cubic-line one the other chat identified. If the normalized cubic coefficient is
\[
A_3(s)=c(s)\,D
\]
for a fixed diagonal-traceless direction \(D\) with
\[
J_0DJ_0=-D,
\]
then reflection-equivariance of the normalized cubic line gives
\[
A_3(-s)=-J_0A_3(s)J_0=c(s)\,D.
\]
But by scalar extraction,
\[
A_3(-s)=c(-s)\,D.
\]
So
\[
c(-s)=c(s).
\]
That is the clean conceptual reason \(c\) should be even. Not a miracle cancellation, and not a full parity theorem for all channels. turn135file0

So my current attack summary is:

- the late-\(v_5\) side is no longer the main problem; it is “sterile or already-quintic”; turn150file0
- the clean branch is no longer blocked by new local geometry; it is blocked by one finite scalar theorem,
  \[
  C_1=C_3=C_5=0;
  \]
- the strongest next move is to go into the actual scalar normalization equations and prove that the scalar extraction commutes with centered reflection through jet \(5\). turn179file2

The source-determinant ratio idea is still valuable, but I now see it as the **backup / below-lifted rigidity language**, not the very first thing to prove. The first thing to prove is the finite scalar descent lemma above. If that falls, the clean mixed-local branch near the centered base is done. Then whatever remains is global/nonlocal capture, not new local mixed geometry.

## The exact attack

The paper still does not expose the raw-to-canonical scalar normalization equations for \(c\), so the full parity-block test cannot yet be run literally from the draft alone. But the draft already gives enough to see that the quintic and septic channels are structurally fine; the only missing block is the scalar one. turn196file4

So the best next move is to introduce and prove these four statements.

### 1. Raw centered jet → canonical package map
Define a finite-jet centered raw one-pair jet space \(R_{\le 5}\) and a normalization map
\[
N_{\le 5}(R)=\bigl(c,\ A_5^{\mathfrak f},\ \Delta_7\bigr),
\]
given by actual normalization equations, not just gauge laws.

Right now the draft gives gauge laws like
\[
A_3^{\mathrm{new}}=A_3,\qquad
A_5^{\mathrm{new}}=A_5+c_2A_3+[B_2,A_3],
\]
and the gauge-invariant residual
\[
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7,
\]
but not the equations that select \(c\) itself from a raw centered jet. That is the missing layer. turn196file8

### 2. Finite-jet uniqueness lemma
Prove that the normalization conditions determine
\[
(c,\ A_5^{\mathfrak f},\ \Delta_7)
\]
uniquely through jet \(5\).

This is the key rigidity input. Without uniqueness, equivariance does not force parity.

### 3. Reflection-sign lemma for the normalization equations
Let
\[
\Sigma(F)(z)=J_0F(-z)J_0.
\]
Prove that, through jet \(5\), the normalization equations transform with the sign pattern

- scalar block: reflection-even,
- fixed-sector quintic block: reflection-odd,
- septic residual block: reflection-odd.

This is exactly the finite block-parity criterion the other chat isolated. The quintic and septic parts are already structurally aligned: the raw quintic ambiguity is anti-fixed/traceless, and \(\Delta_7\) is already even on the centered branch. The only unresolved part is the scalar block. turn196file4

### 4. Scalar descent corollary
Once 1–3 are in place, the cubic-line argument is immediate.

If the normalized cubic coefficient is
\[
A_3(s)=c(s)\,D
\]
for a fixed diagonal-traceless direction \(D\) with
\[
J_0DJ_0=-D,
\]
then reflection-equivariance gives
\[
A_3(-s)=-J_0A_3(s)J_0=c(s)D,
\]
while scalar extraction gives
\[
A_3(-s)=c(-s)D.
\]
Hence
\[
c(-s)=c(s)\pmod{s^6}.
\]

This is the real conceptual reason \(c\) should be even. It is not a miraculous coefficient cancellation. It is cubic-line equivariance. turn196file9

}
\]

}

\[
\boxed{
c(-s)=c(s)\pmod{s^6},

\[

\[

\[
\boxed{
\text{finite-jet scalar descent for the cubic line.}
}
\]

The clean conceptual mechanism is the cubic-line one.

If the normalized cubic coefficient is
\[
A_3(s)=c(s)\,D
\]
with fixed diagonal-traceless \(D\) satisfying
\[
J_0DJ_0=-D,
\]
then any reflection-equivariant scalar normalization rule must satisfy
\[
A_3(-s)=-J_0A_3(s)J_0=c(s)D.
\]
But scalar extraction also gives
\[
A_3(-s)=c(-s)D.
\]
Hence
\[
c(-s)=c(s)\pmod{s^6}.
\]

So the evenness of \(c\) should come from **equivariant cubic-line normalization**, not from a miracle cancellation. That is the actual bottleneck now. 

And that means the remaining mixed-local theorem is even smaller than “prove parity of everything”:

\[
\boxed{
\text{anti-fixed/traceless quintic ambiguity cannot leak into the scalar channel through jet }5.
}
\]

This is exactly consistent with the latest TeX check: the quintic and septic parity channels are structurally already in place, and the only missing block is the scalar normalization block for \(c\).

1. **Local mixed exhaustion near the centered base.**  
   Every sufficiently small nearby mixed \(4\)-point branch is either the clean branch \(V_1\neq 0\), or a late-\(v_5\) branch already sterile or already-quintic. This is now essentially assembled from the right-pincer lemmas. turn188file0

   The scalar normalization/gauge-fixing step commutes with centered reflection through jet \(5\), so
   \[
   C_1=C_3=C_5=0.
   \]

3. **Conclusion.**  
   The clean branch is dead locally, and with it the genuinely new mixed-local geometry near the centered base is exhausted.

So the attack has become ultra-specific:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the only live local failure mode is the scalar normalization/gauge-fixing step.}
}
\]

If the direct scalar-equivariance proof stalls, the right backup is the below-lifted mixed source-ratio route, because that is the correct coupled object that sees both \(Y\) and \(S\). \[

## The attack I ran

I tested whether the latest draft already contains enough to prove that scalar descent.

The result is:

### 1. Quintic channel: structurally fine
The paper/notes already have the centered involution
\[
\Sigma(F)(z)=J_0F(-z)J_0,
\qquad
\Sigma_5(A)=-J_0AJ_0,
\]
and the raw quintic ambiguity is already forced into the \(J_0\)-anti-fixed traceless sector through order \(5\). So the order-\(5\) ambiguity is already in the “wrong channel” to generate scalar leakage by itself. 

### 2. Septic channel: fine
The paper already treats the canonical septic datum as the gauge-invariant residual
\[
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7,
\]
and on the centered branch
\[
u_5,\ v_5,\ u_{7,K_1},\ v_{7,K_1}\ \text{odd},\qquad
\Delta_7\ \text{even}.
\]
So the septic parity block is already in the correct channel. turn203file13

### 3. Scalar channel: this is the only missing block
The latest draft still does **not** expose the raw-to-canonical scalar normalization equations that define \(c\). It gives gauge laws like
\[
A_3^{\mathrm{new}}=A_3,\qquad
A_5^{\mathrm{new}}=A_5+c_2A_3+[B_2,A_3],
\]
and the gauge-invariant \(\Delta_7\), but not the actual equations selecting the scalar \(c\) from a raw centered jet. So the scalar block test is not executable from the paper alone. 

That is the exact bottleneck.

## The clean conceptual mechanism is clear

The right-pincer sharpening is correct. If the normalized cubic coefficient is
\[
A_3(s)=c(s)\,D
\]
for a fixed diagonal-traceless direction \(D\) with
\[
J_0DJ_0=-D,
\]
then reflection-equivariance of the normalized cubic line would give
\[
A_3(-s)=-J_0A_3(s)J_0=c(s)D,
\]
while scalar extraction gives
\[
A_3(-s)=c(-s)D.
\]
Hence
\[
c(-s)=c(s).
\]

So the evenness of \(c\) should come from **equivariant cubic-line normalization**, not from a miraculous coefficient cancellation. 

## Why the new nonmixed ammo matters

It does not close the clean branch directly.

What it does do is tell us what not to waste time on. The no-go lemma says planar \((x,S)\)-only geometry cannot kill the \(4\)-point branch in principle, so the remaining clean-branch theorem cannot come from \(S\)-geometry alone. It has to use either centered parity transfer or genuine coupled \(Y\)–\(S\) source-level structure. The repeated-source/source-determinant viewpoint is therefore the right **backup** language if scalar descent stalls, but it does not remove the scalar bottleneck by itself. 

## Bottom line

The farthest honest push is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The genuinely new mixed-local problem has been reduced to one finite scalar theorem.}
}
\]

and even more sharply,

\[
\boxed{
\text{the only live local failure mode is whether the scalar normalization/gauge-fixing step commutes with centered reflection through jet }5.
}
\]

So: no, I cannot honestly say the proof is completed from the current paper alone.

What I can honestly say is that the mixed-local problem is now cornered so tightly that the remaining obstruction is not geometric anymore. It is one missing scalar-normalization block. If that block is supplied or derived, the clean branch dies, and then the only remaining escape would be global/nonlocal, not a new local mixed septic pattern.

```latex
\begin{remark}[What the four-point branch now reduces to]
```

```latex
(m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,s)=(1,2),\ (1,4),\ (2,5),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,\operatorname{ord}_0\mathcal Z)=(1,1),\ (1,3),\ (2,2),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,\operatorname{ord}_0\mathcal R)=(1,0),\ (1,2),\ (2,1).
\]
Equivalently, in the below-lifted Wronskian formulation from
Remark~\ref{rem:wronskian-order-reformulation-mixed-list}, the dangerous mixed
models are exactly the order-pairs
\[
(\operatorname{ord}_0J_\lambda,\operatorname{ord}_0J_{u_5})
=(1,2),\ (1,4),\ (2,4).
\]
So the mixed low-order branch is already a finite canonical
Wronskian-ratio obstruction problem, captured in local mixed $x$-coordinates by
\[
\kappa_{1,1},\qquad \kappa_{1,3},\qquad \kappa_{2,2}.
\]

By the realization lemma, no identity involving only
\[
(c,v_5,u_5,\Delta_7)
\]
and their derivatives can eliminate these mixed patterns in general.

At the pair level, the centered fixed-sector quintic package
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)=u_5(s)I+v_5(s)S
\]
is the natural object controlling whether any quintic patch opens at all. By
Corollary~\ref{cor:centered-quintic-fixed-sector-nontriviality},
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)\not\equiv 0,
\]
so the centered branch cannot suffer total quintic collapse.

The mixed local picture near the centered base is now sharper than a mere
patch dichotomy. By
Corollary~\ref{cor:right-pincer-local-reduction-centered-base}, every
sufficiently small nearby genuinely new mixed $4$-point obstruction must lie
on the clean branch
\[
\operatorname{ord}_s v_5=1.
\]
Every late-$v_5$ branch is already either locally sterile on the automatic
$u_5$-patch or absorbed into the defect-free planar quintic-circuit regime.
Thus the genuinely new mixed local geometry near the centered base has been
reduced to the single clean branch $V_1\neq 0$.

Accordingly, the remaining mixed-side theorem is no longer another lifted jet
computation, nor a pointwise coefficient nonvanishing statement such as
$V_1\neq 0$ in isolation. It is the finite scalar descent on the clean branch,
namely
\[
c(-s)=c(s)\pmod{s^6},
\qquad\text{equivalently}\qquad
C_1=C_3=C_5=0,
\]
which makes the centered good-$v_5$-patch parity bridge formal. Beyond that,
any further mixed closure must come from global capture or from deeper
source-level corrected quotient-germ structure rather than from the present
lifted variables alone.
\end{remark}
```

## 3) Replace `rem:live-attack-routes`

with:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Live attack routes]
\label{rem:live-attack-routes}
At the present stage, the live routes are now quite sharply separated.

\begin{enumerate}
\item
\textbf{Two-point source-level verification.}
The finite-order criterion is now sharply isolated. It is enough to verify that
the actual corrected two-pair cubic/quintic/septic package is analytic on small
two-atom data and satisfies swap symmetry, one-amplitude collapse, and
diagonal merger
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=(a_1+a_2)F_h.
\]
Once that is done, the quadratic factorization
\[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2
\]
and the exclusion of the two-point bad-core branch on compact good patches
follow formally.

\item
\textbf{Three-point branch (derivative-geometric layer stabilized).}
The lifted three-point side is now the most mature local branch. Shrinking
exact lifted $3$-point circuits are tied to the osculating determinant and
hence to
\[
K_v=0,
\]
the local branch structure at finite-order $K_v$-zeros is completely
classified by parity, and the odd-order branch is blockwise globally rigid on
good $v_5$-patches. Inside the finite-core program, any residual issue there is
boundary exit of the relevant source/target slope-overlap block, not an
internal three-point propagation mechanism.

\item
\textbf{Four-point mixed branch: global capture after local exhaustion.}
Near the centered base, the mixed local picture is now essentially exhausted.
By the right-pincer package, every late-$v_5$ branch is either locally sterile
on the automatic $u_5$-patch or already absorbed into the planar defect-free
quintic-circuit regime. So the only genuinely new mixed local branch left is
the clean branch
\[
V_1\neq 0.
\]
On that clean branch, the remaining theorem is the finite scalar descent
\[
c(-s)=c(s)\pmod{s^6},
\qquad\text{equivalently}\qquad
C_1=C_3=C_5=0,
\]
which makes the centered good-$v_5$-patch parity bridge formal and excludes
\[
(r,\operatorname{ord}_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}.
\]
Thus the remaining mixed burden is no longer local patch classification but
global capture: prove that every relevant mixed branch is forced into this
centered-base local exhaustion theorem. If a below-lifted backup route is
needed, the natural mixed object is a coupled source-minor ratio built from
$u_5$ and $\lambda=\Delta_7/v_5$, rather than planar $(x,S)$-geometry alone.

\item
\textbf{Four-point nonmixed branch via deeper RH-specific identities.}
Generic local geometry already supports nonmixed odd-order exact branch sheets,
so the next theorem there is not a blanket sterility statement but a deeper
RH-specific parity / divisibility theorem forcing extra vanishing of
\[
\mathcal R=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2},
\]
equivalently of the nonmixed obstruction coefficients
\[
z_2,\ z_4,\ z_6.
\]

\item
\textbf{Below-lifted RH-specific identities.}
Since the realization lemma shows that no definitive local closure can come
from the lifted variables alone, any final $4$-point closure theorem must
ultimately come from deeper source-level or matrix-level RH structure. On the
mixed side, the direct remaining target is the scalar descent theorem for the
cubic line; if that stalls, the natural backup object is a coupled source-minor
ratio seeing both $u_5$ and $\lambda=\Delta_7/v_5$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{remark}
```

```latex
\begin{remark}[Stratified lifted local picture]
\label{rem:wip-stratified-lifted-local-picture}
The lifted local obstruction now splits into one closed regime and two genuinely
live regimes.

First, exact shrinking lifted $3$-point circuits concentrate into
\[
K_v=0.
\]
On good $v_5$-patches, this side is now blockwise globally controlled: there is no
infinite-order flatness, even-order $K_v$-zeros are sterile, odd-order
$K_v$-zeros seed exactly one local opposite-side branch, and that branch
continues uniquely on the maximal right monotone-slope block with no interior
common tangent, no source-side return, and no interior accumulation. So the
three-point side contributes only possible boundary exit, not an internal
recurrence mechanism.

Second, exact shrinking lifted $4$-point circuits concentrate into
\[
T_v=0.
\]
On the nonmixed side $K_v\neq 0$, the local derivative-side picture is now
explicit. Exact contacts force zeros of
\[
\mathcal R=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2},
\]
isolated zeros are classified by parity, one-sign $\mathcal R$-intervals are
exactly-contact sterile, recurrent exact contacts force affine-planar collapse,
and repeated-source first loss is completely reduced to diagonal birth at odd
zeros of $\mathcal R$. So the nonmixed $4$-point side is no longer a vague
local branching problem; what remains there is global/source-level control of
which odd zeros of $\mathcal R$ occur on genuine opened arcs.

Third, on the mixed side $K_v=T_v=0$, the low-order obstruction list is now
finite and explicit:
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,s)=(1,2),\ (1,4),\ (2,5),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,\operatorname{ord}_0\mathcal Z)=(1,1),\ (1,3),\ (2,2).
\]
At the pair level, however, the centered quintic fixed-sector package
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)=u_5(s)I+v_5(s)S
\]
is now known not to vanish identically on the centered diagonal branch. Near
the centered base, the right-pincer package further reduces the mixed local
picture: every late-$v_5$ branch is either locally sterile on the automatic
$u_5$-patch or already absorbed into the planar quintic-circuit regime, so the
only genuinely new mixed local branch left there is the clean branch
\[
\operatorname{ord}_s v_5=1.
\]

Thus the remaining lifted local issues are now:
the global/source-level control of odd zeros of $\mathcal R$ on the nonmixed
side, the finite scalar descent
\[
c(-s)=c(s)\pmod{s^6}
\]
on the clean mixed branch, and beyond that the global capture problem forcing
every relevant mixed branch into the centered-base local exhaustion theorem.
\end{remark}
```

```latex
\begin{remark}[Current geometric bottleneck]
\label{rem:current-geometric-bottleneck}
The remaining geometric bottleneck is now split into two qualitatively
different layers.

On the one-pair geometric layer, the obstruction is no longer bulk $W=0$
geometry, and it is no longer local adjacent pair-pair birth across a generic
turning boundary. On the $W=0,\ M\neq 0$ side,
Proposition~\ref{prop:no-W-flat-interval} excludes open-interval flatness and
Theorem~\ref{thm:finite-order-w-zero-local-sterility} shows that every
finite-order isolated $W=0$ boundary is locally sterile for pair-pair birth.
On the turning-boundary side,
Theorem~\ref{thm:adjacent-pair-pair-exclusion-turning} removes actual adjacent
pair-pair lines unconditionally.

At the lifted order-$7$ level, the canonical derivative-geometric determinants
\[
K_v
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
T_v
\]
govern shrinking exact lifted $3$- and $4$-point circuits on
$v_5\neq 0$ patches. On the $3$-point side, this layer is stabilized: shrinking
exact circuits concentrate into $\{K_v=0\}$, finite-order isolated zeros are
classified by parity, and the odd-order branch is blockwise globally rigid on
good $v_5$-patches.

On the $4$-point side, exact shrinking lifted $4$-point circuits concentrate
into
\[
\{T_v=0\},
\]
again with uniform small-diameter exclusion away from that zero set.

On the nonmixed side $K_v\neq 0$, generic odd-order $T_v$-zeros can still
carry preexisting close branches, so the nonmixed branch remains genuinely
live and now asks for global/source-level control of which odd zeros of
\[
\mathcal R=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2}
\]
actually arise on opened arcs.

By contrast, on the mixed side $K_v=T_v=0$, the local geometry near the
centered base is no longer the main bottleneck. There the right-pincer package
shows that every late-$v_5$ branch is either locally sterile on the automatic
$u_5$-patch or already absorbed into the defect-free planar quintic-circuit
regime, so the only genuinely new mixed local branch left is the clean branch
\[
V_1\neq 0.
\]
Accordingly, the mixed bottleneck is no longer a diffuse local codimension-two
analysis but the finite scalar descent
\[
c(-s)=c(s)\pmod{s^6}
\]
on that clean branch, together with the global capture problem of forcing every
relevant mixed branch into this centered-base local regime.

So the missing lifted ingredient is no longer another generic local geometric
exclusion theorem. It is: global/source-level control of odd zeros of
$\mathcal R$ on the nonmixed side; finite scalar descent on the clean mixed
branch; and beyond that the global/nonlocal capture problem linking the finite-core
endgame to this local exhaustion package.
\end{remark}
```

```latex
\begin{remark}[Current state of the argument]
\label{rem:current-state-of-argument}
The local one-pair analysis now consists of the canonical triple
\[
(c(h),\,v_5(h),\,\Delta_7(h)),
\]
together with the derived quantities
\[
M(h)=c(h)v_5'(h)-c'(h)v_5(h),
\qquad
N(h)=c(h)\Delta_7'(h)-c'(h)\Delta_7(h),
\]
\[
L(h)=v_5(h)\Delta_7'(h)-v_5'(h)\Delta_7(h),
\qquad
W(h)=\det(F(h),F'(h),F''(h)).
\]

On the region where $v_5M\neq 0$, the projective graph variables
\[
\mu=\frac{c}{v_5},
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}
\]
identify the normalized curve with a graph $\lambda=\lambda(\mu)$, and
\[
\lambda_{\mu\mu}=\frac{v_5^3}{M^3}W,
\qquad
\beta:=\lambda_\mu=-\frac{L}{M},
\qquad
T(h)=\left(-\frac{L(h)}{M(h)},\frac{N(h)}{M(h)}\right).
\]
Thus the global line-incidence problem is equivalently a problem about the
recurrence of tangent slopes $\beta$, or about vertical-line re-entry on the
dual tangent-line curve $T$.

Locally, both generic boundary types are now under control. At finite-order
$W=0,\ M\neq 0$ boundaries there is no local pair-pair birth, while at
generic turning boundaries actual adjacent pair-pair lines are excluded
unconditionally. The stronger symmetric directional-kernel theorem remains
available only conditionally on zero-capture and now serves as a sharper but
nonessential alternative route.

Accordingly, the remaining gap is no longer local boundary geometry. It is the
global propagation theorem linking these local facts: no fixed finite-slope line
should be able to leave and later re-enter the tangent-slope / tangent-line
data on nonadjacent branches. On the highest-new slice, this is the same as a
no-reentry theorem for the scalar graph
\[
\phi=\lambda^{[1]},
\qquad
\beta^{[1]}=\phi_\mu,
\qquad
m^{[1]}=\phi-\mu\phi_\mu.
\]

On the lifted $4$-point side, the mixed low-order obstruction list is now both
finite and canonical:
\[
(r,\operatorname{ord}_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\},
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,s)=(1,2),\ (1,4),\ (2,5),
\]
equivalently
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6).
\]
Near the centered base, however, the mixed local picture is no longer a free
local classification problem. The right-pincer package reduces every late-$v_5$
branch to one of two absorbed regimes: either it is locally sterile on the
automatic $u_5$-patch, or it is affine-planar and hence already absorbed into
the defect-free planar quintic-circuit regime. Thus the only genuinely new
mixed local branch left there is the clean branch
\[
V_1\neq 0.
\]

So the mixed-side local theorem has been reduced to the finite scalar descent
\[
c(-s)=c(s)\pmod{s^6},
\]
which makes the centered good-$v_5$-patch parity bridge formal. Consequently,
the mixed-side frontier is no longer local patch opening or late-$v_5$
degeneration; it is global capture, namely whether every relevant mixed branch
is forced into this centered-base local exhaustion theorem.

In parallel, the nonmixed side remains a genuinely separate branch: generic
local geometry already supports nonmixed odd-order exact branch sheets, so the
remaining nonmixed burden is deeper RH-specific source-/matrix-level control of
the odd zeros of
\[
\mathcal R=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2},
\]
not another local sterility statement.
\end{remark}
```

```latex
\begin{remark}[Post-draft findings: established, provisional, and live]
\label{rem:post-draft-findings-established-provisional-live}
Since this draft state, six additional conclusions have emerged.

First, on the two-point branch, the exact finite-order source criterion is now
isolated sharply: if the corrected two-pair cubic/quintic/septic package is
source-defined, has one-amplitude collapse, and merges on coincident atoms, then
the exact quadratic factorization
\[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2
\]
follows formally. So the remaining two-point issue is no longer a broad
interaction ansatz, but the specific diagonal-merger/source-definedness theorem
for the corrected two-atom package.

Second, on the lifted four-point branch, the explicit low-order obstruction
list has been reduced to the six coefficients
\[
z_2,\ z_4,\ z_6,\ \kappa_{1,1},\ \kappa_{1,3},\ \kappa_{2,2},
\]
or equivalently to the order patterns
\[
\operatorname{ord}_0\mathcal R\in\{1,3,5\},
\qquad
(r,\operatorname{ord}_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}.
\]

Third, the centered symmetric-placement Taylor package now gives explicit septic
coefficients
\[
D_2,\qquad D_4,\qquad D_6,
\]
explicit bridge coefficients
\[
X_1,X_3,X_5,\qquad L_1,L_3,L_5,
\]
and a punctured-neighborhood exclusion at the diagonal base.

Fourth, the centered fixed-sector quintic package
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)=u_5(s)I+v_5(s)S
\]
is now firmly established as the correct pair-level object on the mixed side.
The centered tagged witness survives specialization strongly enough to show
\[
U_1\neq 0,
\qquad
u_5(s)\not\equiv 0,
\qquad
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)\not\equiv 0,
\]
so the centered quintic pair cannot totally collapse. This yields the
punctured-arc quintic-patch dichotomy on the mixed side.

Fifth, the right-pincer package now sharpens that dichotomy near the centered
base: every late-$v_5$ branch is either locally sterile on the automatic
$u_5$-patch or already absorbed into the planar defect-free quintic-circuit
regime. So the only genuinely new mixed local branch left there is the clean
branch
\[
V_1\neq 0.
\]

Sixth, on that clean branch the remaining theorem has become very small:
the finite scalar descent
\[
c(-s)=c(s)\pmod{s^6},
\qquad\text{equivalently}\qquad
C_1=C_3=C_5=0.
\]
Once this holds, the centered good-$v_5$-patch bridge becomes formal:
\[
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},
\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{cv_5}
\]
are odd through the required order, and the entire explicit mixed low-order
bad list
\[
(r,\operatorname{ord}_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}
\]
is excluded there.

So the present frontier is no longer a generic local geometry problem. It is
the combination of a source-level two-point structure theorem, a finite scalar
descent theorem on the clean mixed four-point branch together with global
capture into the centered-base local exhaustion package, and a deeper
RH-specific identity on the nonmixed four-point branch.
\end{remark}
```
